## Executive Summary

JR Woodward (legal name: Gailand Woodward Jr.) is a church planter, missiologist, and movement leader who has spent more than three decades establishing missional-incarnational communities across the United States. As National Director of the V3 Church Planting Movement, co-founder of Missio Alliance and the Praxis Gathering, and author of three books on missional culture, movement ecclesiology, and leadership, Woodward has become one of the most trusted practitioner-scholars in the North American missional church movement. His work is distinguished by the rare integration of grassroots church planting experience with rigorous academic research -- his most recent book, *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023), is a direct outgrowth of his PhD dissertation at the University of Manchester.

His distinctive contribution is the **synthesis of continental philosophy (Girard, Wink, Stringfellow) with hands-on church planting praxis** -- a combination virtually no other voice in the missional-incarnational movement offers at this depth. Operating as the architect to Alan Hirsch's prophet, Woodward builds carefully named frameworks (Five Culture Creators, Four Spaces of Belonging, Three Contours of Leadership, Eight Movement Competencies) that translate abstract theology into deployable training systems. His body of work progresses from practical culture-building (*Creating a Missional Culture*, IVP 2012) to movement-catalyzing (*The Church as Movement*, IVP 2016, co-authored with Dan White Jr.) to deep diagnostic theology (*The Scandal of Leadership*, 100 Movements 2023), each layer adding sophistication to the same fundamental vision: the church as a neighborhood-rooted, discipleship-fueled, boundary-crossing movement led by many centers rather than one.

Despite his outsized influence -- 7 organizations founded, 9+ board or fellowship roles (per CV), 600+ leaders trained in V3's first decade (CV) with **1,000+** often cited in broader marketing, adjunct teaching across multiple seminaries, IVP Book of the Year 2017 for *The Church as Movement* (also IVP Reader's Choice Award 2016 per CV), ~274 Google Scholar citations -- Woodward's personal digital presence is notably underdeveloped (3.3/5). He has no personal YouTube channel (despite 20-30 videos scattered across third-party platforms), no hosted podcast (despite 11+ guest appearances), a basic WordPress site with no email capture, dormant Instagram, and no online courses on any discoverable platform. His influence is disproportionately embodied -- V3 training cohorts, seminary classrooms, conference stages, and organizational leadership -- rather than digitally captured and centralized. His Substack "Faithful Resistance" (launched 2025) represents an emerging owned-audience strategy but serves a narrower political-prophetic niche rather than his full intellectual range.

The monetization opportunity is estimated at $33K-$118K/year through scaled online courses (digitizing V3 Praxis Cohort curriculum), missing audiobooks for all titles, a centralized YouTube channel, premium Substack tiers, and downloadable frameworks. His audience -- primarily church planters, seminary students, denominational strategists, and abuse-aware communities -- already pays for content through V3 training fees, seminary tuition, conference registration, and book purchases. The large pool of V3-trained planters (600+ in the first decade on CV; **1,000+** in cumulative messaging) represents a warm audience that could be routed into structured content journeys.

The core opportunity for Movemental is to surface, connect, and amplify a substantial body of work that is currently fragmented across 12+ platforms Woodward does not own. His network -- anchored by Alan Hirsch (forewords for 2 books, published through 100Movements), Dan White Jr. (co-author, co-leader of V3), David Fitch (Missio Alliance colleague), and the broader Missio Alliance board -- represents a direct pipeline to additional high-value authors. His frameworks (Five Culture Creators, APEST as cultural environments, Theology of the Powers, mimetic leadership) complement and deepen Hirsch's foundational work, making them a natural paired offering.

## Top 5 Opportunities

1. **Digitize V3 training curriculum**: The 30-week Praxis Cohort and 4 Immersion courses have no public-facing online equivalent. Packaging these as structured courses would surface his most valuable content to a global audience. (HIGH priority, MEDIUM effort)

2. **Centralize video content**: Aggregate 20-30 existing videos from Vimeo, conference channels, and third-party platforms into a single searchable library. Extract short-form clips for Reels/Shorts. (HIGH priority, LOW effort)

3. **Build website-to-Substack funnel**: 15.8K Twitter followers and 6.3K Facebook followers have no email capture pathway. Add newsletter signup to jrwoodward.com, create lead magnet from existing frameworks. (HIGH priority, LOW effort)

4. **Produce audiobooks**: None of his 4 books have audiobook editions. *The Scandal of Leadership* (4.77/5 rating, growing interest in leadership abuse topics) should be first. (HIGH priority, MEDIUM effort)

5. **Launch "Powers & Leadership" course**: Convert PhD research + *Scandal of Leadership* into an online course targeting seminary students and church leaders. Unique niche with no competitor. (HIGH priority, MEDIUM effort)

---

## Movemental Recommendation

**Fit Score**: 7.7/10
**Recommendation**: Onboard -- strong candidate

JR Woodward is the diagnostic builder to Alan Hirsch's prophetic catalyst. His frameworks (Five Culture Creators, Theology of the Powers, mimetic leadership) complement and deepen the foundational APEST/mDNA work that anchors the Movemental platform. His network effects score (9/10) reflects connections to virtually every major figure in the missional movement. The gap between his embodied influence and digital expression is one of the largest in the pipeline -- precisely the problem Movemental solves. His "Faithful Resistance" Substack adds a unique political-prophetic dimension no other Movemental author currently offers.

**Recommended sequencing**: Phase 1 = Woodward + Hirsch + Dan White Jr. (the V3/100Movements core ecosystem)

## 2. PhD thesis (metadata + abstract + structure)

**Full title**: *Missional Leadership, Mimetic Desire, and a Theology of the Powers*  
**Author (thesis title page)**: Gailand A Woodward Jr.  
**Award**: Doctor of Philosophy, University of Manchester, Faculty of Humanities, **2020**  
**School**: School of Arts, Languages and Cultures  
**Research site**: Nazarene Theological College, Manchester  
**Final word count (thesis)**: 80,385 words  
**Dedication**: To the V3 Church Planting Movement  

### Research question (from abstract)

> How might a theology of the Powers help missional leaders to practice a spirituality which reshapes their desires for the sake of discipleship, community, and mission?

### Abstract (condensed from thesis; see PDF for full wording)

All ecclesial leadership exercises power — legitimately through Christ-like holy love, or illegitimately through worldly selfish ambition. The thesis addresses the “fall” of leaders into **domineering** leadership (pride, manipulation, status-seeking, kingdom-building), which hurts people, misrepresents Christ, and damages witness — especially acute for **missional** leadership that claims visible kingdom witness.

Missional literature has raised **imitation** of leaders and human **desire**, and has begun to retrieve **Powers** language, but has not adequately linked these threads. **Walter Wink** (Powers as “domination system”; leaders who mimic the Powers open the church to the demonic) and **René Girard** (imitation and desire tied to the Powers) are combined to build an **imitation-based conceptual framework**: missional leadership ↔ mimetic desire ↔ theology of the Powers. Leaders “fall” when they mimic the Powers through malformed desire; redeemed leadership is **imitating Christ**, reshaping desire toward discipleship, community, and mission. **There is no neutral ground: not to imitate Christ is to imitate the Powers.** Missional leadership is ultimately about being an example worth imitating.

### Chapter outline (from thesis table of contents)

1. **The Challenge of Missional Leadership** — nature of missional leadership; misshaping/reshaping; themes (spirituality, culture/world, imitation); Van Gelder, Roxburgh, etc.  
2. **The Subversion of Leadership** — 1 Peter / Houston; imitation-based framework; three directions of imitation; Powers rediscovery.  
3. **Leadership and the Powers** — Walter Wink: naming, unmasking, engaging; Pauline principalities; domination system; evaluation.  
4. **Leadership and Imitation** — René Girard; mimetic cycle; Powers in James; positive mimesis; evaluation.  
5. **Missional Leadership Worthy of Imitation** — William Stringfellow (image, institution, ideology) mapped to **identity, praxis, telos**; “scandal of leadership”; Christlike imitation; suggestions toward a **catechism** for leader formation.

**Conclusion** — summary, significance (missiological contribution; deeper diagnosis than psychology-only accounts), directions for further study (e.g., ideology in collective life, James K.A. Smith on liturgy and desire, positive mimesis in community), closing prayer for leaders.

### Acknowledgements (names useful for network research)

Supervisor **Phil Meadows**; V3 team **Dan White Jr., Mike Pumphrey, Lori Ruffin, Elice Kim, Matt Alexander, Tonya White**; planters/coaches; **Josh Hayden**, **Guy Wasko**, **Vivek Jones**, **Luke and Lena Glover**, **Won Choi**; NTC colleagues **Thomas Noble**, **Deirdre Brower Latz**, **Julie Lunn**, **Peter Rae**, **Dwight Swanson**, **Paul Hoffmann**, **Tammie Grimm**, **Gift Mtukwa**; **BGAV** (Wayne Faison, John Upton, Laura McDaniel, Marilee White); boards; **Pauline Dawkins-Cole** / international prayer team; **Alan Hirsch** (articles, prayer); **David Fitch**; **Jeremy Chen**; **Taeler Morgan** (editing).

### Relation to book

The thesis is the academic antecedent of *The Scandal of Leadership: Unmasking the Powers of Domination in the Church* (100 Movements Publishing, 2023). The PDF is the authoritative version for citations, methodology, and bibliography prior to trade-book editing.

# Digital Reality Profile: JR Woodward

**Research Date**: January 4, 2026  
**Confidence Level**: High

## Executive Summary

JR Woodward is a church planter, author, and missiologist with over 30 years of experience establishing churches that emphasize tight-knit community, life-forming discipleship, locally-rooted presence, and boundary-crossing mission. He holds a Ph.D. from the University of Manchester (UK) and a Master of Arts in Global Leadership from Fuller Theological Seminary. Woodward has authored 3 books, including "Creating a Missional Culture" (IVP, 2012), co-authored "The Church as Movement" (IVP, 2016), and most recently published "The Scandal of Leadership: Unmasking the Powers of Domination in the Church" (100 Movements Publishing, 2023), which is based on his Ph.D. research.

Woodward currently serves as the National Director for the V3 Church Planting Movement, where he trains church planters across North America. He co-founded the Missio Alliance and Praxis Gathering, and serves as an adjunct professor at Fuller Theological Seminary (leading a Doctor of Global Leadership cohort starting Spring 2025), Central Seminary, and Missio Seminary. He also serves on the boards of Reliant Mission, Movement Leaders Collective, and the Fuller Global Mission Advisory Council.

Woodward's digital presence includes a personal website (jrwoodward.com), an Academia.edu profile, multiple organizational platforms (V3, Missio Alliance, Praxis Gathering), publisher platforms (InterVarsity Press, 100 Movements Publishing), and academic affiliations. His content spans books, organizational training materials, academic courses, and conference speaking. The content ecosystem shows strong thematic consistency around missional culture, church as movement, and leadership, though opportunities exist for greater content interconnection and digital amplification of embodied work.

**Key Findings**:
- Established author with 3 published books (1 solo, 1 co-authored, 1 recent solo based on Ph.D. research)
- Over 30 years of practical church planting experience combined with academic credentials (Ph.D.)
- National Director of V3 Church Planting Movement (training church planters across North America)
- Co-founder of significant missional organizations (Missio Alliance, Praxis Gathering)
- Adjunct professor at multiple seminaries (Fuller, Central, Missio)
- Board service on multiple missional organizations
- Recent publication (2023) indicates active writing and research
- Strong integration of academic research and practical experience

**Primary Opportunities**:
- Content repurposing (books → articles/courses, teaching → articles/courses, training → articles/courses)
- Content series development from books, teaching, and 30+ years of experience
- Content interconnection across multiple platforms
- Digital amplification of conference talks, seminary teaching, and training materials
- Unified content platform for discoverability and network effects

**Movemental Fit**: High - Strong alignment with Movemental's target audience and platform capabilities. Woodward's work (30+ years church planting experience, published author, National Director, co-founder of missional organizations, adjunct professor) aligns perfectly with Movemental's focus on Christian movement thought leaders. Opportunities for content repurposing, series development, and network effects.

## Current Digital Presence

### Website Presence

**Primary Website**: jrwoodward.com (active, official personal website)

**Organizational Websites**:

<a id="profile-biography"></a>

<!-- SOURCE: docs/movement_leader_research/jr-woodward/profile/biography.md -->

# Biography: JR Woodward

**Status**: Complete
**Last updated**: 2026-04-13

---

## Narrative Biography

JR Woodward is a church planter, missiologist, and movement leader who has spent more than three decades establishing missional-incarnational communities across the United States. As the National Director of the V3 Church Planting Movement, co-founder of Missio Alliance and the Praxis Gathering, and author of three books on missional culture, movement ecclesiology, and leadership, Woodward has become one of the most trusted practitioner-scholars in the North American missional church movement. His work is distinguished by the rare integration of grassroots church planting experience with rigorous academic research -- his most recent book, *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023), is a direct outgrowth of his PhD dissertation at the University of Manchester.

Woodward's church planting journey began in 1989 when he founded New Life Christian Fellowship (NLCF) at Virginia Tech in Blacksburg, Virginia, as part of Great Commission Ministries. In the first five years of that plant, he experienced both the loneliness of pioneering leadership and the difficulty of cultivating missional hearts in an inherited congregation. NLCF grew to become a significant campus and community presence; by 2007, the church had branched into two congregations -- one serving Virginia Tech students and another serving the broader New River Valley community. During the Virginia Tech shooting of 2007, the church played a visible role in the campus community's response, with two members among those killed and ten others directly connected to the church.

Around 2003, Woodward and other NLCF members planted Kairos Los Angeles, a network of neighborhood churches in the East Hollywood area. This move to Los Angeles deepened Woodward's commitment to incarnational, neighborhood-rooted ministry. He lived in East Hollywood and served on the East Hollywood Neighborhood Council, embodying his conviction that the church should be embedded in the fabric of its local community rather than operating as an institution set apart from it. He co-founded several additional organizations during this period: the Solis Foundation (focused on walking alongside the poor in Lodwar, Kenya), the Ecclesia Network, and eventually Missio Alliance and the Praxis Gathering -- an annual conference of over three hundred on-the-ground missional practitioners.

Woodward pursued academic work alongside his planting. He holds a B.S. in psychology from Radford University (1987), an M.A. from Fuller Theological Seminary in missional leadership (2011) with a thesis titled *Equippers as Environmentalist: Re-imaging Leadership in Today's Western Church*, and in 2020 completed a PhD at the University of Manchester (research based at Nazarene Theological College) supervised by Phil Meadows, examined internally by Joseph Wood and externally by Wilbert Shenk. His dissertation, *Missional Leadership, Mimetic Desire, and a Theology of the Powers* (~80,400 words), synthesized Walter Wink, René Girard, and William Stringfellow to develop an imitation-based framework for domineering leadership and Christ-shaped alternative. Colleagues including Dwight Swanson at NTC gave formative feedback on the project. The work was published in adapted form as *The Scandal of Leadership* in 2023. His first book, *Creating a Missional Culture* (IVP, 2012), introduced the concept of polycentric leadership and the five "culture creators" -- Dream Awakeners, Heart Revealers, Story Tellers, Soul Healers, and Light Givers -- as a practical application of Ephesians 4 ministry. His second, *The Church as Movement* (IVP, 2016), co-authored with Dan White Jr. and with a foreword by Alan Hirsch, outlined eight competencies for creating movemental churches rooted in neighborhoods.

Today, Woodward serves as National Director of the V3 Church Planting Movement, where he trains church planters across North America and internationally in what he calls "grounded spirituality, missions theology, and movement ecclesiology." He leads V3 collaboratively with Dan White Jr. and Jesse Eubanks, embodying the shared leadership model he advocates. He serves as an adjunct professor at Central Seminary, Missio Seminary, and American Evangelical University, and sits on multiple boards including Missio Alliance, Reliant Mission, Fuller's Global Mission Advisory Council, Fuller's Church Initiatives Board, and KINEO. He currently serves locally with the District Church in Washington, DC. Outside of ministry, Woodward is a surfer, skateboarder, photographer, and film enthusiast who attends the Sundance Film Festival whenever possible.

## Origin & Formation

JR Woodward's full legal name is Gailand Woodward Jr., as recorded in his University of Manchester PhD thesis. No public information is available about his birth date, birthplace, or early life. His career in ministry began in 1989 with the founding of NLCF at Virginia Tech, suggesting he was likely in his twenties at that time. His about.me profile and self-description consistently emphasize his identity as someone who "encourages people to participate in God's renewal of all things" -- a missional and activist orientation that has been consistent from his earliest public work.

His formative years as a church planter at Virginia Tech shaped his understanding of the difficulties of cultivating missional culture. He has spoken publicly about the loneliness of those early years and the challenge of inheriting a congregation without a missional heart. This experience became the laboratory for the frameworks he would later develop in *Creating a Missional Culture*.

## Key Relationships & Influences

| Person | Relationship | Significance |
|--------|-------------|-------------|
| Alan Hirsch | Mentor-figure, endorser | Wrote the foreword for both *Creating a Missional Culture* and *The Church as Movement*. Hirsch praised Woodward's work as containing "missiological insights that only an apostolically inclined leader can bring." Both operate in the missional-incarnational stream; Woodward applies and extends Hirsch's APEST framework. |
| Dan White Jr. | Co-author, co-leader | Co-authored *The Church as Movement*; co-leads V3 alongside Woodward. Both share commitment to neighborhood-rooted, movement-oriented church planting. |
| Jesse Eubanks | V3 co-leader | Collaborates with Woodward and White in leading V3 Movement. |
| Walter Wink | Intellectual influence (posthumous) | Wink's trilogy on "the Powers" (naming, unmasking, engaging) is foundational to Woodward's theology of institutional power. |
| Rene Girard | Intellectual influence (posthumous) | Girard's mimetic desire theory is central to Woodward's PhD thesis and *The Scandal of Leadership*. |
| William Stringfellow | Intellectual influence (posthumous) | Stringfellow's framework of Image, Institution, and Ideology shapes Woodward's analysis of how powers manifest in church systems. |
| Oscar Romero | Exemplar figure | Used as a primary case study of Christlike, kenotic leadership in *The Scandal of Leadership*. |
| Phil Meadows | PhD supervisor | University of Manchester — primary supervisor for the doctoral thesis. |
| Joseph Wood; Wilbert Shenk | PhD examiners | Internal and external examiners (per CV). |
| Dwight Swanson | Doctoral interlocutor | Nazarene Theological College colleague; thanked in thesis acknowledgements for academic feedback. |
| David Fitch | Theological ally | Contributed to *The Scandal of Leadership*; fellow missional theologian. |
| Preston Sprinkle | Platform amplifier | Hosted Woodward on *Theology in the Raw* podcast for extended conversation on leadership and power. |

## In Their Own Words

> "The unholy use of power has damaged the church's witness, crippled her mission, and aided her decline." -- *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023), via [100Movements](https://www.100movements.org/books/scandal-of-leadership-jr-woodward)

> "Will we become a scandal to those who look to us as leaders, or will we choose to imitate the scandalous way of Christ?" -- *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023), via [100Movements](https://www.100movements.org/books/scandal-of-leadership-jr-woodward)

> "Missional communities are a sent people who connect with God, do life together and receive power from the Holy Spirit to partner with God to accomplish his purposes in our neighborhoods and in the world." -- Verge Network article, via [vergenetwork.org](https://vergenetwork.org/jr-woodward-what-is-a-missional-community-printable/)

> "If we choose not to imitate Christ, by default we are choosing to imitate the powers." -- cited in Goodreads reviews of *The Scandal of Leadership*

> "Not to imitate Christ is to imitate the Powers." -- PhD thesis core argument, via [University of Manchester Research Explorer](https://research.manchester.ac.uk/en/studentTheses/missional-leadership-mimetic-desire-and-a-theology-of-the-powers)

## Disambiguation

JR Woodward (Gailand Woodward Jr.) is a distinctive figure in the missional church movement. There are no significant public-figure name collisions that would cause confusion, though note:

1. **JR Woodward (church planter, missiologist)** -- THIS IS OUR SUBJECT. National Director of V3 Church Planting Movement, author of *Creating a Missional Culture*, co-founder of Missio Alliance, PhD from University of Manchester. Known online as @dreamawakener.

2. **Bob Woodward (journalist)** -- Unrelated. The famous Watergate journalist and *Washington Post* associate editor.

3. **Various other Woodwards** -- No other "JR Woodward" with a significant public profile in Christian ministry or missiology.

**Reliable disambiguation modifiers**: "missional," "V3," "church planter," "Creating a Missional Culture," "Missio Alliance," "@dreamawakener," "polycentric leadership."

<a id="profile-theology"></a>

<!-- SOURCE: docs/movement_leader_research/jr-woodward/profile/theology.md -->

# Theological Profile: JR Woodward

**Status**: Complete
**Last updated**: 2026-04-12

---

## Core Thesis

The Western church has adopted worldly patterns of power and domination that damage its witness, cripple its mission, and fuel the epidemic of fallen leaders. Recovery requires two interrelated moves: (1) cultivating a polycentric, shared leadership culture rooted in the full fivefold ministry of Ephesians 4, and (2) practicing a self-emptying spirituality grounded in the imitation of Christ rather than the imitation of the Powers. The church is fundamentally a movement -- neighborhood-rooted, discipleship-fueled, boundary-crossing -- and its leadership must reflect the kenotic, communal character of the triune God.

## Theological Tradition

**Primary**: Missional-incarnational theology, rooted in post-Christendom missiology and practical theology

**Secondary influences**: Anabaptist-adjacent ecclesiology (emphasis on community, peace, incarnational presence), Wesleyan-Methodist tradition (PhD at University of Manchester through Nazarene Theological College / Manchester Wesley Research Centre), liberation theology motifs (Oscar Romero as exemplar, Solis Foundation work with the poor in Kenya), and charismatic movement dynamics (studied rather than personally claimed)

**Denominational context**: Has operated across denominational lines throughout his career. Founded NLCF as part of Great Commission Ministries; V3 has ties to Virginia Baptists. Not bound to a single tradition; works with church planters from multiple backgrounds.

## Key Frameworks & Models

| Framework | Description | Where Developed |
|-----------|-------------|----------------|
| **Polycentric Leadership** | Leadership structured around "many centers that interrelate" rather than hierarchical (top-down) or flat (undifferentiated) models. Reflects the communal nature of the triune God. Activates the priesthood of all believers more effectively than CEO-pastor models. | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012) |
| **Five Culture Creators** | Woodward's practical application of Ephesians 4:11 APEST gifts, each renamed to emphasize their culture-shaping function: Apostle = **Dream Awakener**, Prophet = **Heart Revealer**, Evangelist = **Story Teller**, Pastor = **Soul Healer**, Teacher = **Light Giver**. Each creates a distinct environment within missional culture. | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012) |
| **Five Environments** | Five cultural environments that a healthy missional community cultivates: (1) Learning, (2) Healing, (3) Welcoming, (4) Liberating, (5) Thriving. Each environment corresponds to one of the five culture creators. | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012) |
| **The Cultural Web** | Six interconnected dimensions that shape congregational and neighborhood culture: Language, Artifacts, Rituals, Ethics, Institutions, Guiding Narratives. Leaders must understand all six to cultivate missional culture. | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012) |
| **Five Cultural Megashifts** | Five macro-level transitions that missional leaders must navigate: (1) Media: print/broadcast to digital, (2) Philosophy: modernity to postmodernity, (3) Science: classical to emergent, (4) Geography: rural to urban, (5) Religion: Christendom to post-Christendom. | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012) |
| **Eight Movement Competencies** | Eight necessary competencies for creating movemental, neighborhood-rooted churches. Framework for church planter training in V3. | *The Church as Movement* (2016, with Dan White Jr.) |
| **Four Spaces of Belonging** | A framework for understanding how discipleship and mission happen across four relational spaces of varying intimacy and size. | Articles and teaching; [V3 Movement](https://thev3movement.org/2014/01/14/discipleship-and-the-four-spaces-of-belonging/) |
| **Theology of the Powers** | A robust synthesis drawing on Walter Wink (spiritual powers embodied in systems), Rene Girard (mimetic desire and scapegoating), and William Stringfellow (Image, Institution, Ideology as categories of how powers operate). Argues that principalities and powers are created good but fallen and redeemable, while Satan/demonic forces are emergent realities without redemptive possibility. | PhD thesis (2020), *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023) |
| **Imitation-Based Leadership Framework** | Leaders are inescapably imitative beings (per Girard). When they imitate worldly power models, they become domineering; when they imitate Christ's kenotic self-emptying, they become life-giving servants. "Not to imitate Christ is to imitate the Powers." | PhD thesis (2020), *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023) |
| **Three Contours of Leadership** | Framework for diagnosing leadership health: (1) Identity -- who leaders are, (2) Praxis -- how they lead and relate, (3) Telos -- what they value and pursue. Domineering leaders malform across all three. | *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023) |

## Distinctive Positions

- **Polycentric over hierarchical or flat**: Woodward rejects both top-down hierarchy (CEO-pastor) and undifferentiated flat structures, advocating instead for multiple interrelated centers of leadership. This reflects Trinitarian theology -- God's own communal nature.
- **APEST as culture creators, not just roles**: The fivefold gifts are not merely leadership offices but culture-shaping vocations. Each creates a distinct environment (learning, healing, welcoming, liberating, thriving) necessary for a fully missional community.
- **Domineering leadership is a theological problem, not just a psychological one**: The epidemic of fallen church leaders cannot be adequately diagnosed through psychology or management theory alone. It requires a theology of the Powers that understands how spiritual forces operate through institutional systems.
- **Mimetic desire shapes leaders unconsciously**: Drawing on Girard, Woodward argues that desires are not self-generated but are formed through models. Leaders who unconsciously absorb worldly models of power will inevitably reproduce domination, regardless of their stated theology.
- **Church as neighborhood-rooted movement**: The church should be locally embedded, not institutionally detached. Woodward himself served on a neighborhood council; V3 trains planters to root churches in specific neighborhoods.
- **Kenotic leadership as the alternative**: The solution to domineering leadership is not better management but self-emptying (kenotic) spirituality that reshapes desires through the imitation of Christ. Oscar Romero serves as Woodward's primary exemplar.
- **Christendom's corporate adoption distorts ecclesial practice**: Woodward traces how Christianity moved from "a fellowship in Palestine, a philosophy in Greece, an institution in Rome, a government in Europe, and an enterprise in America" -- and argues that the corporate-enterprise model must be dismantled in favor of movement ecclesiology.
- **"Being" precedes "doing" in mission**: Missional identity must be established before missional action. God changes people by changing their identity, their sense of self-definition, before calling them to particular tasks.

## Intellectual Genealogy

**Shaped by**:
- **Walter Wink** -- Theology of the Powers; naming, unmasking, and engaging principalities embodied in systems; the "Domination System" as a spiritual-structural reality
- **Rene Girard** -- Mimetic desire theory; triangular desire (we desire what our models desire); scapegoat mechanism; Jesus as the one who reveals and disrupts the scapegoating pattern
- **William Stringfellow** -- Prophetic resistance to the Powers; analysis of how powers manifest through Image, Institution, and Ideology; the "power of resurrection" against the "power of death"
- **Oscar Romero** -- Exemplar of kenotic, Christlike leadership under persecution; positive model of resisting the Powers through self-emptying service
- **Lesslie Newbigin** -- Post-Christendom missiology (shared influence with Alan Hirsch)
- **James K.A. Smith** -- Cultural liturgies and the formation of desire (referenced in reviews of *Creating a Missional Culture*)
- **Henri Nouwen** -- Spiritual formation and pastoral identity (cited in *Creating a Missional Culture*)
- **Miroslav Volf** -- Theology of embrace and reconciliation (cited in *Creating a Missional Culture*)

**In conversation with**:
- Alan Hirsch (closest senior collaborator; wrote forewords for two of Woodward's books; shared APEST/missional movement framework)
- Dan White Jr. (co-author, co-leader of V3)
- David Fitch (fellow missional theologian; contributor to *The Scandal of Leadership*)
- Amos Yong (Pentecostal theologian; contributor to *The Scandal of Leadership*)
- Preston Sprinkle (extended podcast conversation on leadership and power)
- Jesse Eubanks (V3 co-leader)

**Pushes back against**:
- **CEO-pastor / hierarchical leadership**: The concentration of power in a single senior leader, which Woodward sees as a corporate import that distorts biblical ecclesiology and creates conditions for abuse.
- **Attractional church model**: The "come and see" paradigm that builds institutions rather than embedding in neighborhoods. Woodward advocates incarnational, "go and be" presence.
- **Surface-level diagnosis of leadership failure**: Approaches that treat fallen leaders as individual moral failures without examining the systemic, spiritual, and mimetic forces that shape desire and behavior.
- **Christendom assumptions**: The default assumption that the church occupies a privileged cultural position. Woodward works from a post-Christendom, missionary posture.
- **Shepherd-Teacher dominance**: Like Hirsch, Woodward argues that the Western church has marginalized apostolic, prophetic, and evangelistic functions in favor of pastoral care and teaching -- creating an imbalanced, maintenance-oriented church.

## Theological Evolution

Woodward's theology has developed through three distinct phases, each building on the previous:

1. **Missional culture phase (2003-2012)**: Rooted in his Virginia Tech and Los Angeles church planting experience, Woodward developed his practical theology of polycentric leadership, the five culture creators, and the cultural web. *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012) is the primary output. The focus is on how to build missional communities from the inside out -- culture as the unseen force that shapes a church's effectiveness more than vision or strategy.

2. **Movement ecclesiology phase (2012-2016)**: Working with Dan White Jr. and deepening his involvement with V3, Woodward expanded from individual church culture to the dynamics of church-planting movements. *The Church as Movement* (2016) outlines the competencies needed for movement multiplication. The shift is from "how do we make one church missional?" to "how do we catalyze a movement of missional churches?"

3. **Power, desire, and imitation phase (2016-2023)**: Woodward's PhD research marked a significant deepening into the theological roots of leadership failure. Drawing on Wink, Girard, and Stringfellow, he moved from the practical-constructive (what healthy leadership looks like) to the diagnostic-prophetic (why leaders fall and what spiritual forces are at work). *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023) represents his most theologically sophisticated work. The turn toward desire formation and mimetic theory adds a dimension absent from his earlier work.

Throughout all three phases, Woodward's commitment to neighborhood-rooted, incarnational, movement-oriented ecclesiology has remained constant. The progression is from practical culture-building to movement-catalyzing to deep diagnostic theology -- each layer adding depth to the same fundamental vision.

---

<a id="profile-voice-analysis"></a>

<!-- SOURCE: docs/movement_leader_research/jr-woodward/profile/voice-analysis.md -->

# Voice Analysis: JR Woodward

**Status**: Complete
**Last updated**: 2026-04-12
**Sources analyzed**: Verge Network articles, Missio Alliance articles (Parts II and III of *The Scandal of Leadership* series), V3 Movement blog posts, *Theology in the Raw* podcast appearance, *Faith in a Fresh Vibe* podcast appearance, Goodreads reviews of all three books, book descriptions and sample chapters.

---

## Voice Summary

JR Woodward writes and speaks as a practitioner-scholar -- someone whose theological frameworks emerge from decades of grassroots church planting rather than from the academy alone. His voice is characterized by methodical, framework-heavy thinking delivered in an accessible but sometimes dense register. He is more systematic builder than prophetic provocateur: where Alan Hirsch leads with urgency and disruption, Woodward leads with careful diagnosis and structured alternatives. His tone is pastoral-academic -- warm toward fellow practitioners, sharp toward systems of domination, and consistently oriented toward practical application. He is at his most distinctive when renaming familiar concepts with evocative language (apostles become "dream awakeners," prophets become "heart revealers") and when integrating continental philosophy (Girard, Wink) with hands-on church planting wisdom.

## Writing Characteristics

| Dimension | Assessment |
|-----------|-----------|
| Register | Accessible academic -- integrates scholarly concepts (mimetic desire, kenosis, principalities and powers, cultural web) with clear definitions and practical applications. More academic than Hirsch's popular writing; more accessible than a typical dissertation. Varies by context: Missio Alliance articles skew more scholarly; V3 Movement posts skew more pastoral-practical. |
| Complexity | Moderate to High -- builds multi-layered frameworks with systematic rigor. His books are framework-dense: five culture creators, five environments, six cultural web dimensions, five megashifts, eight movement competencies. Some reviewers note the density can become repetitive or jargon-heavy ("polycentric," "telos," "mimetic desire"). His PhD-derived work (*The Scandal of Leadership*) is the most complex; *Creating a Missional Culture* is the most accessible. |
| Tone | Diagnostic-Constructive -- combines careful analysis of what is wrong (domineering leadership, corporate church models, power abuse) with structured proposals for what could be (polycentric leadership, kenotic spirituality, missional culture). Less prophetically urgent than Hirsch; more methodically constructive. Occasionally passionate when addressing leadership abuse. |
| Storytelling | Moderate -- uses concrete examples and analogies (Swiss government structure, jazz ensembles, geese flight formations) to illustrate abstract concepts. Less reliant on personal narrative than Hirsch. Historical examples (Oscar Romero, early church, Bill Hybels/Mark Driscoll as cautionary tales) serve as evidence for theological arguments. |
| Humor | Minimal in writing -- Woodward's written work is earnest and substantive. No significant use of humor, irony, or self-deprecation in published articles or book excerpts. Spoken interviews show slightly more warmth but still primarily substantive. |
| Scripture Use | Strategic and foundational -- Ephesians 4:11-13 is the anchor text for his entire APEST/culture-creators framework. Uses Jesus' words (John 20:21, Matthew 5:14-16) and Pauline epistles to ground identity before action. Reads Paul through a Girardian lens (Philippians as kenotic leadership text). Does not proof-text; integrates biblical theology with sociological and philosophical argument. Emphasizes Hebraic reading: identity before imperative, narrative before proposition. |

## Signature Patterns

- **Recurring phrases**:
  - "missional-incarnational" (his signature compound descriptor, shared with the broader movement)
  - "dream awakener" (his self-identifier and term for the apostolic function)
  - "polycentric leadership" (multiple centers that interrelate)
  - "tight-knit community, life-forming discipleship, locally-rooted presence, boundary-crossing mission" (his four-part descriptor for healthy churches; appears verbatim across multiple bios)
  - "a sign, foretaste, and instrument of God's kingdom" (his ecclesiological vision statement)
  - "grounded spirituality, missions theology, and movement ecclesiology" (his three-part descriptor for V3's approach)
  - "the Powers" (capitalized; spiritual forces embodied in institutional systems)
  - "not to imitate Christ is to imitate the Powers" (his central thesis from PhD work)
  - "sent people" (identity-before-action framing for missional communities)
  - "God's renewal of all things" (eschatological frame for mission)

- **Favorite metaphors and analogies**:
  - **Iceberg**: Surface symptoms (fallen leaders) hide deeper structural and spiritual causes beneath the waterline. Woodward consistently insists on deeper diagnosis before solutions.
  - **Cultural web**: Culture is an interconnected web of six dimensions (language, artifacts, rituals, ethics, institutions, narratives) -- pull one strand and others move.
  - **Dream awakener**: The apostle does not plant churches so much as awaken dormant dreams of God's kingdom. Evocative, poetic reframing of a role often described in purely organizational terms.
  - **Jazz ensemble**: Polycentric leadership functions like a jazz group -- multiple players with distinct voices contributing to a unified whole, rather than a conductor directing an orchestra.
  - **Geese in formation**: Shared leadership as rotating headship, each member taking turns leading.
  - **Swiss government**: Polycentric governance as an alternative to both monarchy and anarchy.

- **Argument structure**: Woodward typically builds a case through:
  1. **Careful framing** -- establishes the core question (often citing Einstein: "spend fifty-five minutes determining the proper question")
  2. **Diagnosis of the current problem** -- what the church has inherited from Christendom, corporate culture, or worldly power models
  3. **Theological grounding** -- Scripture and scholarly sources (Wink, Girard, Stringfellow) that illuminate the deeper dynamics
  4. **Framework introduction** -- a named model with clear categories (five culture creators, three contours of leadership, cultural web)
  5. **Practical implications** -- what this means for church planters, leaders, and communities
  6. **Invitation** -- a quieter, more reflective call to action than Hirsch's prophetic urgency; often framed as a question ("Will we become a scandal to those who look to us as leaders, or will we choose to imitate the scandalous way of Christ?")

- **Opening style**: Tends to open with a diagnostic observation or a framing question rather than a provocative declaration. Establishes the problem before offering the solution. More methodical than dramatic.

- **Identity-first methodology**: A consistent hallmark -- Woodward always establishes who we are (identity, sentness, calling) before describing what we do (practices, structures, strategies). "God changes us by changing our identities, our sense of self-definition."

- **Renaming as reframing**: Woodward's most distinctive rhetorical move is taking familiar theological categories and giving them fresh, evocative names. Apostles become dream awakeners; prophets become heart revealers. This is not mere branding -- it is an intentional strategy to help practitioners see familiar roles through a culture-shaping lens rather than a hierarchical one.

## Sample Passages

> "Missional communities are a sent people who connect with God, do life together and receive power from the Holy Spirit to partner with God to accomplish his purposes in our neighborhoods and in the world." -- [Verge Network](https://vergenetwork.org/jr-woodward-what-is-a-missional-community-printable/)

> "The unholy use of power has damaged the church's witness, crippled her mission, and aided her decline." -- *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023)

> "Will we become a scandal to those who look to us as leaders, or will we choose to imitate the scandalous way of Christ?" -- *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023)

> "Christianity started out in Palestine as a fellowship, became a philosophy in Greece, an institution in Rome, a government in Europe, and an enterprise in America." -- [Missio Alliance article](https://www.missioalliance.org/polycentric-missional-leadership-j-r-woodward/) (quoting a common attribution, used to frame his argument)

> "A critical but often overlooked part of that narrative is how the fall not only affected humanity but also social and cosmic realities." -- [Missio Alliance, Scandal of Leadership Part III](https://missioalliance.org/developing-an-imitation-based-framework-of-healthy-leadership-in-christ-the-scandal-of-leadership-part-iii/)

> "If we choose not to imitate Christ, by default we are choosing to imitate the powers." -- cited in multiple reviews of *The Scandal of Leadership*

## Speaking vs. Writing

Based on podcast appearances (*Theology in the Raw*, *Faith in a Fresh Vibe*):

- **More conversational and warm**: In spoken contexts, Woodward is more relaxed and relational than in his writing. He engages with interviewers genuinely, builds on their questions, and allows for tangents that reveal his broader thinking.
- **Same systematic architecture**: Whether speaking or writing, the same frameworks (polycentric leadership, mimetic desire, the Powers) are present. He cannot help but organize ideas into categories and models.
- **More concrete examples**: In conversation, he reaches for vivid analogies (Swiss government, jazz, geese) more readily than in his denser written work.
- **Scholarly yet accessible**: Interviewers and reviewers consistently note his ability to make complex theological and philosophical concepts (Girard's mimetic theory, Wink's Powers trilogy) understandable for church practitioners. His spoken style is described as "thoughtful" and "scholarly yet accessible."
- **Less prophetically urgent than Hirsch**: Where Hirsch's spoken voice rises with passion and prophetic fire, Woodward's tends toward careful, measured analysis. He is the diagnostician rather than the prophet -- equally concerned about the same problems, but approaching them with the precision of a researcher rather than the urgency of an agitator.
- **Quiet conviction**: His spoken style carries a calm but deep conviction. He does not raise his voice or pound the table; he builds his case methodically and lets the evidence speak.

The overall effect is that Woodward's voice -- written and spoken -- is that of a builder-diagnostician: someone who constructs careful frameworks, names what is wrong with precision, and offers structured alternatives grounded in both Scripture and the best of contemporary scholarship. He is the architect to Hirsch's prophet.

## Comparison with Alan Hirsch

| Dimension | JR Woodward | Alan Hirsch |
|-----------|-------------|-------------|
| Rhetorical mode | Diagnostic-constructive | Prophetic-apostolic |
| Opening move | Framing question or diagnostic observation | Provocative declaration or sharp diagnosis |
| Framework density | Very high (5 culture creators, 5 environments, 6 cultural web dimensions, 5 megashifts, 3 contours, etc.) | High (6 mDNA elements, APEST, but fewer sub-frameworks) |
| Storytelling | Moderate; analogies and case studies | Heavy; personal narrative, historical movements, contemporary examples |
| Humor | Minimal | Occasional; dry, self-deprecating Australian humor |
| Urgency | Measured, methodical | High; "the church must change or die" |
| Intellectual sources | Continental philosophy (Girard, Wink, Stringfellow) | Anthropology (Turner), missiology (Newbigin, Allen), organic systems theory |
| Self-identifier | "Dream awakener," "church planter, activist, missiologist" | "Movement catalyst," prophetic-apostolic voice |
| Signature move | Renaming (apostle = dream awakener) | Binary contrasts ("not X but Y") |
| Tone toward institutions | Diagnostic; names systemic power dynamics | Prophetically critical; "institution vs. movement" |

Both share the same fundamental missional-incarnational vision and both build on Ephesians 4 APEST. Woodward is the practitioner-scholar who applies and extends Hirsch's frameworks with additional academic rigor and practical specificity; Hirsch is the movement catalyst who provides the overarching prophetic vision. Their collaboration (Hirsch writing forewords for Woodward's books) reflects this complementary dynamic.

## Digital Presence Score: JR Woodward

| Dimension | Score (1-5) | Notes |
|-----------|-------------|-------|
| Website Quality | 2.5 | WordPress/Astra site is functional but basic; lacks modern engagement features (no prominent newsletter CTA, no embedded video, limited interactivity); legacy domain fragmentation (jrwoodward.com, .net, .me, .blogspot) |
| Social Media Activity | 3 | Active on X (~15.8K) and Facebook (~6.3K author page), but not a high-volume poster; no meaningful Instagram/TikTok/YouTube personal strategy; V3 org accounts provide supplementary reach |
| Content Freshness | 3.5 | Substack "Faithful Resistance" is active with bi-weekly posts (2025-2026); V3 blog contributes; books are the primary content form; Substack content is notably current and engaged |
| Platform Diversity | 4 | Strong presence across organizational sites (V3, Missio Alliance, 100M, Praxis Gathering), academic platforms (Academia.edu, 4 seminary adjunct roles), publisher pages, conference profiles, and podcast guest spots |
| Email/Newsletter | 3 | Substack exists with paid tier — ahead of many peers; "hundreds" of subscribers is modest but the publication is relatively new; no email capture on main website |
| Discoverability (SEO) | 3.5 | Multiple organizational profiles, publisher pages, Amazon, Goodreads, Academia.edu, and conference profiles provide solid SEO signals; no Wikipedia page (gap vs. Hirsch); ranks well for "JR Woodward missional" queries |
| **Overall** | **3.3/5** | Strong organizational and academic web presence with a distinctive Substack voice, but personal digital engagement platforms (website, social, video) are underdeveloped relative to his influence and institutional reach |

### Score Interpretation

JR Woodward has a **broad institutional presence with an emerging content voice**. His influence is felt most strongly through:
- His **organizational role** (V3 Movement, National Director) which carries his training methodology to 1,000+ planters
- His **published books** which are well-rated (4.25 avg on Goodreads) and distributed across retail/library platforms
- His **academic credibility** (PhD Manchester, 4 adjunct roles, Academia.edu profile with 477 followers)
- His **Substack** which represents a distinct, more politically-engaged voice drawing from his doctoral research

### Key Gaps for Movemental to Address

1. **No centralized YouTube/video presence** — significant content scattered across Seminary Now, V3, and conference channels
2. **Modest personal social following** — 15.8K on X and 6.3K on Facebook; V3 org channels supplement but don't replace personal brand
3. **Website underperforms** — WordPress/Astra is functional but lacks the polish expected for an author of his stature; no newsletter CTA, no book showcase, no embedded media
4. **No Wikipedia page** — unlike Alan Hirsch; represents a discoverability gap
5. **No hosted podcast** — only guest appearances despite strong audio/teaching presence
6. **Instagram dormant** — handle @dreamawakener exists but minimal activity
7. **Domain fragmentation** — jrwoodward.com, .net, .me, and .blogspot create confusion; need consolidation
8. **No free lead magnet** — no downloadable resource to drive email list growth
9. **Newsletter list building** — "hundreds" of subscribers is early; no visible funnel from website or social to Substack

### Comparative Note (vs. Alan Hirsch)

| Dimension | JR Woodward | Alan Hirsch |
|-----------|-------------|-------------|
| Twitter/X Followers | ~15,800 | ~37,900 |
| Facebook | ~6,300 (author page) | ~14,000 + 6,800 |
| Substack Subscribers | Hundreds | 1,500+ |
| Goodreads Ratings | 650 (4.25 avg) | 16,762 (varies) |
| Academia.edu | 477 followers, 8 papers | Not found |
| Wikipedia | No | Yes |
| Assessment Tools | No | Yes (APEST) |
| Org Website Quality | V3: Squarespace (good) | Multiple: 100M, 5Q, Forge (good) |
| Personal Website | WordPress/Astra (basic) | Squarespace (clean) |
| Newsletter Platform | Substack (clean URL) | Substack (alanhirsch1) |
| Books | 3 authored + forewords | 15+ titles |
| Overall Score | 3.3/5 | 3.2/5 |

**Notable**: Despite fewer total followers and books, Woodward scores slightly higher overall due to his active Academia.edu profile, more substantive Substack content, and cleaner platform handle consistency (@dreamawakener across platforms, jrwoodward.substack.com).

---

## Cross-Platform Observations

1. **Primary platform**: Twitter/X (@dreamawakener, ~15.8K) is the most established personal social account
2. **Consistent handle**: @dreamawakener used across X, Instagram, and Flickr — strong personal brand identity
3. **Author page vs personal**: Facebook split between @missionalculture (author page, ~6.3K) and @jr.woodward1 (personal)
4. **Content distribution**: Social media is used primarily to amplify content published elsewhere (Substack, V3 site, conference appearances) rather than as primary content creation
5. **Video gap**: No centralized personal YouTube presence despite significant video content on Seminary Now and conference channels
6. **Instagram gap**: Handle exists but appears dormant or minimally active — notable gap
7. **Organizational amplification**: V3 Movement has broad social coverage (Facebook, Instagram, YouTube, Threads, Bluesky, TikTok) which extends JR's reach even without personal accounts on those platforms
8. **Professional presence**: LinkedIn confirms identity and organizational roles
9. **Photography interest**: Flickr account under dream-awakener reflects personal interest in photography (also noted in bios: "enjoys photography")

# Newsletter & Email: JR Woodward

**Status**: Complete
**Last updated**: 2026-04-12
**Researcher**: Claude Code

---

## Newsletter

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Platform | Substack |
| Name | Faithful Resistance |
| Subscribe URL | https://jrwoodward.substack.com/ |
| About URL | https://jrwoodward.substack.com/about |
| Tagline | "A Movement of Hope as Technocrats, Autocrats, and Oligarchs Remake the World in Their Image" |
| Frequency | Approximately bi-weekly (2-3 posts per month) |
| Subscribers | Hundreds (specific number not publicly disclosed; Substack shows "hundreds of subscribers") |
| Free/Paid | Free articles with optional paid tier ($10/month or $100/year) |
| Launch | Approximately early-mid 2025 (described as "launched a year ago" in 2026 search results) |

### Content Focus

The newsletter explores faithful Christian witness and resistance in an era of concentrated power. Core themes include:

- Grounded spirituality and hope-filled imagination
- Naming and unmasking the Powers (drawing from Walter Wink, William Stringfellow)
- Discerning how to embody the Way of Jesus amid technocratic, autocratic, and oligarchic pressures
- Learning from historical examples of faithful resistance
- Cultivating courage for present-day action
- Prophetic discipleship and justice

### Author Bio (from Substack)

"Writer | Speaker | Catalyst | Mobilizer | Adjunct Professor | V3 National Director"

### Recent Posts (2025-2026)

| Title | Date | Topic |
|-------|------|-------|
| "Re-Centering" | January 5, 2026 | Stepping away to remain faithful; spiritual renewal |
| "Prophetic Discipleship: Love on Trial" | Late 2025 | Faithfulness under pressure |
| "Faithful Witness as Resistance" | May 27, 2025 | Christian witness as form of resistance |
| "Exposing the Powers" | April 25, 2025 | How Powers distort communities and capacity to love |
| "Hope That Resists" | April 2025 | Hope as an act of resistance |
| "The Engine of Autocracy" | April 2025 | Structural analysis of autocratic power |
| "Unmasking the Spirit of the Age" | March-April 2025 | Cultural discernment |
| "The Power of the 3.5%" | March-April 2025 | Nonviolent resistance movements and critical mass |
| "Authoritarianism is a Spiritual Crisis" | April 7, 2025 | Theological framing of political authoritarianism |
| "Naming and Unmasking the Powers" | April 2, 2025 | Foundation essay drawing from PhD research |
| "Faithful Resistance in the Age of Manufactured Kings" | March 26, 2025 | Opening thesis for the newsletter's mission |

### Content Style

- Long-form theological reflections with practical action orientation
- Draws heavily from PhD research on Powers and Principalities
- Academic rigor (Walter Wink, Rene Girard, Lesslie Newbigin, N.T. Wright) made accessible
- Justice-oriented — connects missional theology to contemporary political realities
- Invites reader participation through comments and discussion
- Distinct from his other writing (books, V3 blog) — more politically engaged and prophetic in tone

### Substack Recommendations (Substacks JR recommends)

| Publication | Author | Focus |
|-------------|--------|-------|
| Today's Edition Newsletter | Robert Hubbell | News through the lens of hope |
| Musing on Life and Faith | Rob Yackley | Faith reflections in a turbulent world |
| A Public Witness | Word&Way | Faith, culture, and politics |
| A Church for the World | Rob Fairbanks | Church reoriented around mission |
| The Low-Level Theologian | Dr. A.J. Swoboda | Theological devotional |
| Gospel and Culture | Timothy Black | Faith and culture through a gospel lens |
| Corey J Widmer | Corey Widmer | Depth, wholeness, wisdom for faithful presence |
| Fitch's Provocations | David Fitch | Power, ideology, subjectivity, culture, and mission |
| StarfishyoU | StarfishyoU | Decentralized, disciple-making leadership |
| Right Side Up | Danielle Strickland | Subversive ideas, disruptive thoughts, spiritual depth |

## Contributing to Other Publications

| Publication | URL | Type | Status |
|-------------|-----|------|--------|

| newchurches.com | newchurches.com | Contributor articles | Active (referenced in bio) |

| Gospel Centered Discipleship | (blog) | Contributor | Referenced in bio |

---

## Observations

1. **Substack is the primary newsletter channel** — "Faithful Resistance" is a substantive publication with bi-weekly cadence and a clear theological-political thesis
2. **Clean handle**: jrwoodward.substack.com — secured the primary vanity URL (unlike Alan Hirsch who has alanhirsch1)
3. **Paid tier available** — $10/month or $100/year indicates intent to monetize, though most content appears free
4. **Modest but growing audience** — "hundreds of subscribers" is early-stage but the newsletter launched relatively recently (~2025)
5. **Distinct content niche** — the newsletter's focus on Powers, resistance, and justice is more politically engaged than his books, which focus on missional ecclesiology and leadership
6. **PhD-powered content** — the newsletter directly leverages his doctoral research on Powers and Principalities, giving it academic depth unusual for Substack
7. **Cross-platform amplification** — Substack posts are shared on X/Twitter and Facebook
8. **Recommendation network** — his Substack recommendations reveal his intellectual community: David Fitch, Danielle Strickland, A.J. Swoboda, Word&Way
9. **Gap**: The personal website (jrwoodward.com) does not prominently feature newsletter signup, creating a missed opportunity to convert website visitors to email subscribers
10. **Gap**: No free lead magnet or downloadable resource identified to drive email signups

# JR Woodward — Complete Bibliography

**Catalog Date**: 2026-04-12
**Status**: Verified from multiple sources (Amazon, Goodreads, IVP, 100 Movements, MWRC, Christianbook.com)

---

## Authored Books

### 1. Creating a Missional Culture: Equipping the Church for the Sake of the World

| Field | Detail |
|---|---|
| **Full Title** | Creating a Missional Culture: Equipping the Church for the Sake of the World |
| **Series** | Forge Partnership Books |
| **Author** | JR Woodward |
| **Foreword** | Alan Hirsch |
| **Publisher** | IVP Books (InterVarsity Press) |
| **Publication Date** | June 28, 2012 |
| **Pages** | 224 |
| **Format — Print** | Paperback (ISBN-10: 0830836535 / ISBN-13: 978-0830836536) |
| **Format — eBook** | Kindle / ePub (ISBN-13: 978-0830866793) |
| **Format — Audiobook** | Not confirmed |
| **Amazon URL** | https://www.amazon.com/Creating-Missional-Culture-Equipping-Church/dp/0830836535 |
| **Goodreads URL** | https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13645227-creating-a-missional-culture |
| **Goodreads Rating** | 4.04 / 5 (242 ratings, 34 reviews) |
| **IVP URL** | https://www.ivpress.com/creating-a-missional-culture |

**Description**: Woodward offers a radical revisioning of church structure, moving beyond incremental adjustments to propose a polycentric leadership model organized around five biblical equipping roles from Ephesians 4:11-13. He reframes these as Dream Awakeners (apostles), Heart Revealers (prophets), Story Tellers (evangelists), Soul Healers (pastors), and Light Givers (teachers). The framework emphasizes creating missional communities equipped to engage their world rather than operating through hierarchical, personality-driven structures. Blends cultural analysis, leadership formation, congregational empowerment, and missional engagement.

---

### 2. The Church as Movement: Starting and Sustaining Missional-Incarnational Communities

| Field | Detail |
|---|---|
| **Full Title** | The Church as Movement: Starting and Sustaining Missional-Incarnational Communities |
| **Authors** | JR Woodward and Dan White Jr. |
| **Foreword** | Alan Hirsch |
| **Publisher** | IVP Books (InterVarsity Press) |
| **Publication Date** | 2016 |
| **Pages** | 256 |
| **Dimensions** | 10.00 x 7.00 inches |
| **Format — Print** | Paperback (ISBN-10: 0830841334 / ISBN-13: 978-0830841332) |
| **Format — eBook** | Kindle / ePub (ISBN-13: 978-0830893621) |
| **Format — Audiobook** | Not confirmed |
| **Retail Price** | $31.99 |
| **Amazon URL** | https://www.amazon.com/Church-Movement-Sustaining-Missional-Incarnational-Communities/dp/0830841334 |
| **Goodreads URL** | https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27414517-the-church-as-movement |
| **Goodreads Rating** | 4.32 / 5 (163 ratings) |
| **IVP URL** | https://www.ivpress.com/the-church-as-movement |
| **Companion Website** | https://churchasmovement.com/ |
| **Award** | IVP Book of the Year 2017 |

**Description**: A practical guide to starting missional-incarnational communities reflecting the viral movement of the early New Testament church. Built around eight necessary competencies: Movement Intelligence, Polycentric Leadership, Being Disciples, Making Disciples, Missional Theology, Ecclesial Architecture, Community Formation, and Incarnational Practices. Features an interactive format with tools, exercises, reflection questions, and activities — designed for church planting teams or discipleship groups to work through together.

---

### 3. The Scandal of Leadership: Unmasking the Powers of Domination in the Church

| Field | Detail |
|---|---|
| **Full Title** | The Scandal of Leadership: Unmasking the Powers of Domination in the Church |
| **Author** | JR Woodward |
| **Foreword** | David Fitch |
| **Afterword** | Amos Yong |
| **Publisher** | 100 Movements Publishing |
| **Publication Date** | April 19, 2023 (paperback); hardcover reissue August 30, 2025 |
| **Pages** | 418 |
| **Format — Print** | Paperback / Hardcover (ISBN-10: 1955142246 / ISBN-13: 978-1955142243) |
| **Format — eBook** | Available |
| **Format — Audiobook** | Not confirmed |
| **Amazon URL** | https://www.amazon.com/Scandal-Leadership-Unmasking-Powers-Domination/dp/1955142246 |
| **Goodreads URL** | https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/136187930-the-scandal-of-leadership |
| **Goodreads Rating** | 4.77 / 5 (73 ratings, 46 reviews) |
| **Publisher URL** | https://www.100movements.org/books/scandal-of-leadership-jr-woodward |
| **Based on** | PhD dissertation, University of Manchester (UK) |

**Description**: Based on Woodward's PhD research, this book addresses the epidemic of leadership failures in churches by offering a comprehensive diagnosis of power abuses and the critical role of imitation. Drawing on Scripture and the scholarship of Walter Wink, Rene Girard, and William Stringfellow, as well as positive examples such as Oscar Romero, the book develops a robust theology of the Powers (Satan, the demonic, principalities and powers). The central thesis proposes an imitation-based framework: leaders either mirror Christ's self-emptying example or unconsciously replicate the fallen world's power structures.

---

### 4. ViralHope: Good News from the Urbs to the Burbs (and Everything in Between)

| Field | Detail |
|---|---|
| **Full Title** | ViralHope: Good News from the Urbs to the Burbs (and Everything in Between) |
| **Role** | Editor |
| **Foreword** | Scot McKnight |
| **Publisher** | Ecclesia Press |
| **Publication Date** | April 4, 2010 |
| **Pages** | Not confirmed |
| **Format — Print** | Paperback (ISBN-10: 0982623607 / ISBN-13: 978-0982623602) |
| **Amazon URL** | https://www.amazon.com/ViralHope-Good-Burbs-Everything-Between/dp/0982623607 |
| **Goodreads URL** | https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7996868-viralhope |
| **Goodreads Rating** | 3.70 / 5 (20 ratings) |

**Description**: An edited collection of short essays by fifty authors from around the world, each answering the question: "What is the gospel for your city?" Contributors include David Fitch, Jonathan Wilson-Hartgrove, Jon Tyson, Christine Sine, Jonathan Dodson, and others. Weaves a tapestry of the gospel across diverse urban and suburban contexts.

---

## Key Training Frameworks (Developed by Woodward)

These frameworks recur across V3 training, books, and teaching:

| Framework | Source | Description |
|---|---|---|
| **Eight Core Competencies** | *The Church as Movement* | Movement Intelligence, Polycentric Leadership, Being Disciples, Making Disciples, Missional Theology, Ecclesial Architecture, Community Formation, Incarnational Practice |
| **Five Equippers** | *Creating a Missional Culture* | Dream Awakeners (apostles), Heart Revealers (prophets), Story Tellers (evangelists), Soul Healers (pastors), Light Givers (teachers) — from Ephesians 4:11-13 |
| **Four Spaces of Belonging** | V3 training / blog | Framework for discipleship through different relational spaces; applied to how Jesus made and multiplied disciples |
| **Theology of the Powers** | *The Scandal of Leadership* | Diagnostic framework for understanding domineering leadership via Wink, Girard, Stringfellow; imitation-based alternative |

# JR Woodward — Academic Papers, Dissertations & Lectures

**Catalog Date**: 2026-04-12  
**Last updated**: 2026-04-13 (PhD thesis PDF + CV on file in [../pdf/](../pdf/); index [../primary-documents.md](../primary-documents.md))  
**Status**: Verified from primary PDFs, Academia.edu, MWRC, Google Scholar, and web sources

---

| **M.A.** | Fuller Theological Seminary | Missional Leadership; **June 2011**; thesis *Equippers as Environmentalist: Re-imaging Leadership in Today's Western Church* (advisor Dr. Robert Freeman) — per CV |

---

## Ph.D. Dissertation (full text on file)

| Field | Detail |
|---|---|
| **Repository copy** | [pdf/phd-thesis-missional-leadership-mimetic-desire-theology-of-the-powers.pdf](../pdf/phd-thesis-missional-leadership-mimetic-desire-theology-of-the-powers.pdf) (217 pp.) |
| **Title** | *Missional Leadership, Mimetic Desire and a Theology of the Powers* |
| **Author (title page)** | Gailand A Woodward Jr. |
| **Institution** | University of Manchester — Faculty of Humanities; School of Arts, Languages and Cultures |
| **Research site** | Nazarene Theological College, Manchester |
| **Year** | 2020 |
| **Supervisor** | Dr. Phil Meadows |
| **Examiners** | Internal: Dr. Joseph Wood; External: Prof. Wilbert Shenk (per CV) |
| **Dedication** | To the V3 Church Planting Movement |
| **Published as Book** | *The Scandal of Leadership: Unmasking the Powers of Domination in the Church* (100 Movements Publishing, 2023) — trade adaptation of the thesis |
| **Key scholars** | Walter Wink; René Girard; William Stringfellow; interlocutors across scripture, missional leadership literature (Van Gelder, Roxburgh, Fitch, etc.) |
| **Research question** | How might a theology of the Powers help missional leaders practice a spirituality that reshapes their desires for the sake of discipleship, community, and mission? |
| **Central claim** | Domineering leadership is tied to mimicking the Powers through malformed desire; redeemed leadership is **imitating Christ** — *there is no neutral ground: not to imitate Christ is to imitate the Powers*; missional leadership is ultimately about being an example worth imitating. |
| **Chapter arc** | (1) Missional leadership challenge; (2) Subversion of leadership — 1 Peter / Houston, imitation-based framework; (3) Leadership & Powers (Wink); (4) Leadership & imitation (Girard); (5) Missional leadership worthy of imitation (Stringfellow: image / institution / ideology ↔ identity, praxis, telos) plus catechism-style suggestions. |

### Abstract (from thesis; abridged)

All ecclesial leadership exercises power — either legitimately (Christ-like holy love) or illegitimately (selfish ambition). The thesis addresses leaders’ “fall” into **domineering** patterns (pride, manipulation, status, empire-building), which wound people and the church’s witness, especially where leaders claim a **missional** identity. Missional literature has surfaced imitation, desire, and Powers language, but not integrated them. **Wink** links leaders who mimic the Powers to the demonic and the “domination system”; **Girard** ties imitation and desire to the Powers. Together they yield an **imitation-based framework** connecting missional leadership, mimetic desire, and a theology of the Powers. Redeemed leadership reshapes desire toward discipleship, community, and mission through **positive mimesis** of Christ.

Wright, René Girard, William Stringfellow, Eugene Peterson, Sarah Coakley, Oscar Romero, Walter Wink.

# JR Woodward -- Video & Multimedia Content Catalog

**Research date:** 2026-04-12
**Subject:** JR Woodward (Dr. J.R. Woodward, PhD) -- church planter, missiologist, National Director of V3 Church Planting Movement
**Status:** Comprehensive catalog based on web research; URLs verified at time of research

---

## Executive Summary

JR Woodward does **not** appear to have his own YouTube channel. His video content is scattered across third-party platforms: conference recording channels (Verge Network / Exponential), organization sites (V3 Movement, Missio Alliance), podcast video channels (Theology in the Raw, The Roys Report), Vimeo (Five Equippers series), and Seminary Now (gated educational content). He also has a growing presence through his Substack "Faithful Resistance" which hosts webinars.

- **Own YouTube channel:** No dedicated channel found
- **Twitter/X handle:** @dreamawakener
- **Facebook:** @missionalculture
- **Substack:** jrwoodward.substack.com ("Faithful Resistance")
- **Estimated total videos across all platforms:** 25-40
- **Date range:** 2011 (earliest confirmed) to 2025-2026 (ongoing)
- **Most viewed:** Likely the Verge Network / Exponential 2011 conference talks and Five Equippers Vimeo series, given their longevity and platform reach

---

## Key Themes Across Video Content

1. **Polycentric / APEST Leadership** -- Five Equippers model (Apostle, Prophet, Evangelist, Pastor, Teacher) as alternative to hierarchical or flat church leadership
2. **Missional Culture** -- Equipping the whole church for mission, not just professional clergy
3. **Church as Movement** -- Moving from institutional "industrial complex" models to missional-incarnational communities
4. **Scandal of Leadership / Domineering Power** -- Unmasking powers of domination in the church (based on PhD research)
5. **Faithful Resistance** -- Prophetic discipleship, resisting technocratic and autocratic powers (2025-2026 emphasis)
6. **Neighborhood-Grounded Church Planting** -- Practical models from Kairos Los Angeles and V3 network

---

---

## Notable Gaps

1. **No dedicated YouTube channel** -- Unlike many peers, Woodward has not centralized his video content
2. **jrwoodward.net domain expired** -- His original website (which linked to the Five Equippers video series and other content) has been lost; jrwoodward.com appears to be the current site
3. **Exponential conference recordings** -- He has spoken at Exponential multiple times but only 2011 recordings are confirmed online
4. **No known TED/TEDx talks**
5. **No known long-form lecture series** (beyond Seminary Now gated content)
6. **V3 Movement site content fragile** -- Some older V3 pages return 404 errors

---

## Comparison to Similar Leaders

JR Woodward's video footprint is notably smaller than peers like Alan Hirsch or Mike Breen, who have extensive YouTube presence through Forge, 5Q, and 3DM channels. Woodward's content is more dispersed and relies heavily on third-party platforms (podcast interviews, conference recordings). His 2023 book launch for "The Scandal of Leadership" generated the largest cluster of video/audio interviews in his career.

# Audio & Podcast Content: JR Woodward

**Research Date**: April 12, 2026
**Confidence Level**: Medium-High
**Researcher**: Movemental Research Team

---

## Summary

JR Woodward does **not host his own podcast**. He is exclusively a **guest** on other shows, with a concentrated burst of appearances in 2023-2025 tied to the release of *The Scandal of Leadership* (Spring 2023). He also maintains a Substack newsletter ("Faithful Resistance") but it is text-only with no audio component identified.

- **Total guest appearances found**: 11 confirmed podcast episodes + 1 video talk + 1 video interview series
- **Total hosted episodes**: 0 (no own podcast identified)
- **Date range**: October 2011 (earliest video) to March 2025 (most recent confirmed)
- **Peak activity**: 2023 (book launch for *The Scandal of Leadership*)

---

---

## Key Themes Across Appearances

### Primary Themes (appear in 5+ episodes)

1. **The Scandal of Leadership / Domineering leadership** — the central thesis of his 2023 book and PhD research; discussed in nearly every appearance from 2023 onward
2. **Polycentric leadership** — the alternative to hierarchical, CEO-model church leadership; drawn from Ephesians 4 five-fold framework
3. **Mimetic desire and scapegoating** (Rene Girard) — how rivalry and imitation drive leadership dysfunction
4. **Powers and principalities** (Walter Wink, William Stringfellow) — systemic spiritual analysis of institutional power

### Secondary Themes (appear in 2-4 episodes)

5. **Four spaces of belonging** — Woodward's framework for community structure
6. **Christlike servant leadership / self-emptying spirituality** (kenosis)
7. **Missional culture and discipleship** — creating communities oriented toward mission
8. **Kingdom vs. brand** — churches focused on God's kingdom rather than institutional growth

### Book-Specific Themes

- **Creating a Missional Culture** (2012): Five equippers, cultural architects, polycentric leadership, missional ethos
- **The Church as Movement** (2016): Movement ecclesiology, missional-incarnational communities, theology of place
- **The Scandal of Leadership** (2023): Powers of domination, mimetic theory, hierarchical vs. polycentric structures, leadership failures

---

|---|---|---|
| Rohadi Nagassar | 2 (two-part series) | Faith in a Fresh Vibe |
| Preston Sprinkle | 1 | Theology in the Raw |

| Cynthia Anderson | 1 | DMMs Frontier Missions / Dare to Multiply |

| Terri Elton & Dwight Zscheile | 1 | Pivot Podcast |

No single host has featured Woodward more than once (aside from the two-part Faith in a Fresh Vibe series).

---

## Gaps & Opportunities

### What Was Not Found

- **No own podcast** — Woodward does not host or co-host any podcast series
- **No audiobook** versions of his books were confirmed (would need to check Audible/Amazon separately)
- **No sermon archives** — no public sermon repository identified (SermonAudio, church website archives, etc.)
- **No Spotify or Apple Podcasts artist profile** — his appearances are distributed across other shows' feeds
- **Limited pre-2022 podcast presence** — despite publishing *Creating a Missional Culture* in 2012 and *The Church as Movement* in 2016, very few podcast appearances from that era were discoverable

### Opportunities for Movemental

1. **Podcast launch potential** — Woodward has no owned audio channel; a Movemental-hosted podcast or interview series could fill this gap
2. **Transcript corpus** — at least one episode (Theology in the Raw) has a public transcript; others may be obtainable for content mining
3. **Thematic consistency** — his message is remarkably consistent (anti-domination, polycentric, kenotic leadership), making him easy to position in content strategy
4. **Active Substack** — "Faithful Resistance" (jrwoodward.substack.com) is his primary owned content channel; cross-promotion with audio content would be natural

---

# JR Woodward: Collaborators Network

**Research Date**: 2026-04-12
**Last Updated**: 2026-04-12

## Co-Authors & Writing Collaborators

| Name | Relationship | Context | Key Details |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Dan White Jr.** | Co-Author | "The Church as Movement" (IVP, 2016) | Co-leads Axiom Church in Syracuse, NY. Works as consultant and missional coach with V3 Movement. They have trained church planters all over North America together. White also authored "Subterranean" (for which Woodward wrote the foreword). |
| **Alan Hirsch** | Foreword Writer, Network Partner | Wrote forewords for "Creating a Missional Culture" (2012) and "The Church as Movement" (2016) | Founder of 100Movements, Forge Mission Training Network, and Future Travelers. Woodward published "The Scandal of Leadership" through Hirsch's 100Movements Publishing. Both serve in the Movement Leaders Collective ecosystem. Hirsch called Woodward's work "peppered with the kind of missiological insights that only an apostolically inclined leader can bring." |
| **David Fitch** | Foreword Writer, Board Colleague | Wrote foreword for "The Scandal of Leadership" (2023) | B.R. Lindner Chair of Evangelical Theology at Northern Seminary. Founding pastor of Life on the Vine Christian Community. Fellow Missio Alliance Board of Trustees member. Endorsed "Creating a Missional Culture." |
| **Amos Yong** | Foreword Writer | Wrote foreword for "The Scandal of Leadership" (2023) | Prominent Pentecostal theologian and scholar. |

## Missio Alliance Network (Co-Founded by Woodward)
