| **Michael Frost** | Morling College, Sydney | Endorsed "The Scandal of Leadership": "Every Christian leader should read this." |
| **Soong-Chan Rah** | Fuller Theological Seminary (Robert Munger Professor) | Endorsed "The Scandal of Leadership." Called it "a leadership-paradigm-shifter." |
| **Daniel Im** | Author, church leader | Endorsed "The Scandal of Leadership": "Finally! An academically robust and comprehensive missiological study..." |
| **Darrell Guder** | Princeton Theological Seminary (Winters Luce Professor) | Endorsed "Creating a Missional Culture": praised its "tested and validated experience as an equipper of the missional church." |
| **Dr. MaryKate Morse** | George Fox Evangelical Seminary | Endorsed "Creating a Missional Culture": praised "fresh views about leadership and church culture." Fellow Missio Alliance board member. |
| **Alan Roxburgh** | The Missional Network | Endorsed "The Church as Movement": praised it as "a simple, intensely practical guide" for moving beyond the "religious industrial complex." |
| **Kevin & Christine Sweeney** | Imagine Church, Honolulu | Endorsed "The Church as Movement." |
| **Dan White Jr.** | Axiom Church, Syracuse | Endorsed "The Scandal of Leadership": "a leadership-paradigm shifter." |

## Other Connections

| Name | Context | Nature |
|---|---|---|
| **Len Tang & Charles E. Cotherman** | Co-editors of "Sent to Flourish" (IVP Academic, 2019) | Woodward contributed the chapter "What Would God's Reign Look Like In Our Neighborhood? Jesus, the Kingdom and the Church." |
| **Rohadi** | Faith in a Fresh Vibe Podcast | Podcast interviewer (2-part series on "The Scandal of Leadership," 2023). |

## Key Relationship Clusters

### The Missional-Incarnational Circle
Woodward sits at the intersection of several overlapping networks:
- **100Movements / Movement Leaders Collective**: Alan Hirsch's ecosystem. Woodward serves on MLC council and publishes through 100M.
- **Missio Alliance**: Co-founded by Woodward. Connects him to David Fitch, Deb Hirsch, MaryKate Morse, Leroy Barber, Jo Anne Lyon, and others.
- **V3 Movement**: Woodward's primary operational role. Connected to Dan White Jr. and Eun Strawser.
- **Forge Mission Training Network**: Alan and Deb Hirsch's training network. Woodward's "Creating a Missional Culture" is in the Forge Partnership Books series.
- **Fuller Theological Seminary**: Academic home connecting to Soong-Chan Rah, the Global Mission Advisory Council, and Church Initiatives Board.

### Mentorship / Influence Lines
- **Alan Hirsch** appears to be a key mentor/endorser figure (forewords for 2 books, published through his imprint).
- **David Fitch** is a close theological ally (foreword, shared board service, Northern Seminary base).
- **Dan White Jr.** is the primary collaborative partner (co-author, V3 coach, mutual endorsement).

## Event Network Summary

### Primary Event Ecosystems
1. **V3 Movement / Praxis Gathering**: Woodward's home base. Annual conference + ongoing immersion trainings.
2. **Missio Alliance**: Co-founded. Regular contributor to alliance gatherings and content platform.
3. **100Movements / Movement Leaders Collective**: Connected through publishing and council membership.
4. **Seminary Circuit**: Fuller, Central, Missio Seminary teaching roles.
5. **Podcast Circuit**: Multiple appearances promoting "The Scandal of Leadership" (2023-2024).

### Geographic Reach
- **Primary base**: Washington DC area (current) / Los Angeles (Kairos LA)
- **National**: North America-wide through V3 Movement
- **International**: Africa, Asia through V3 network; UK through University of Manchester connection
- **Founding work**: Blacksburg, VA (Virginia Tech) through Los Angeles, CA

### Event Frequency Assessment
- **High frequency**: V3 immersion trainings (multiple per year), Substack newsletter (regular)
- **Annual**: Praxis Gathering
- **Periodic**: Conference speaking (Awakenings, Exponential), podcast appearances
- **Ongoing**: Seminary teaching (3 institutions)

### "Creating a Missional Culture" (IVP, 2012)

**Foreword by**: Alan Hirsch

| Endorser | Affiliation | Quote / Summary |
|---|---|---|
| **Alan Hirsch** (Foreword) | 100Movements, Forge | "Peppered with the kind of missiological insights that only an apostolically inclined leader can bring." "JR Woodward has developed an excellent heuristic for leaders to actually make Ephesians 4 a living reality in the local churches." |
| **Darrell Guder** | Princeton Theological Seminary (Winters Luce Professor of Missional and Ecumenical Theology) | "The growing exploration of the theology and practice of the missional church is enriched by this volume. Its authority rests in the author's tested and validated experience as an equipper 'of the missional church for the sake of the world.'" |

His book Creating a Missional Culture reflects all of that. Read it and explore what leading can be in the strange new worlds of mission in North America." |
| **Dr. MaryKate Morse** | George Fox Evangelical Seminary (Professor of Leadership & Spiritual Formation) | "JR Woodward's fresh views about leadership and church culture and his practical guides and suggestions make this a relevant and important book for every congregation. The chapters on polycentric leadership alone are worth the price of the book." |

In this book, JR Woodward uses compelling theology, cultural insight, biblical wisdom and practical examples on how to shift from consumerism to mission..." |

# Press Coverage & Media Mentions: JR Woodward

**Research Date**: 2026-04-12
**Subject**: JR Woodward -- church planter, missiologist, author, National Director of V3 Movement
**Confidence Level**: High (primary sources verified via web search)

---

## Summary

JR Woodward's media presence centers on the missional church ecosystem rather than mainstream Christian media. His coverage is concentrated in: (1) podcast interviews discussing his books, (2) articles on missional/church-planting platforms, (3) news coverage of his V3 leadership role, and (4) seminary/conference speaking features. He has not received significant coverage in mainstream outlets like Christianity Today or Relevant Magazine based on available evidence.

## Creating a Missional Culture (IVP, 2012)

### Published Reviews

| # | Source | Reviewer | Rating | Date | Key Quote | URL |
|---|--------|----------|--------|------|-----------|-----|
| 1 | Themelios (TGC) | Matt Kottman | Mixed | 2013-04-26 | "Rightly notices that churches need to proactively create a culture that centers on mission" but "leans more to being driven by praxis instead of theology" | https://www.thegospelcoalition.org/themelios/review/creating-a-missional-culture-equipping-the-church-for-the-sake-of-the-world/ |
| 2 | EMQ (Missio Nexus) | Jonathan K. Dodson | Positive | 2013-04-01 | "A worthwhile read that provides a gracious, yet prophetic corrective to individualistic, pastor-centric churches" | https://missionexus.org/creating-a-missional-culture-equipping-the-church-for-the-sake-of-the-world/ |
| 3 | Daniel Im (blog) | Daniel Im | 5/5 | 2013-03-31 | "Easy to read, extremely accessible, and has important gems that will help any and every leader cultivate and create a missional culture" | https://www.danielim.com/2013/03/31/book-review-creating-a-missional-culture-jr-woodward/ |
| 4 | Scott Boren (blog) | Scott Boren | Positive | 2013-02-15 | "A great introduction to how culture works within a church setting... will challenge your assumptions while providing practical steps forward" | http://scottboren.blogspot.com/2013/02/creating-missional-culture-by-jr.html |
| 5 | Life and Leadership | Dr. Carlus Gupton | Positive | 2012 (updated 2022) | "One of the most thorough developments" of the APEST leadership framework | http://www.lifeandleadership.com/book-summaries/woodward-creating-a-missional-culture.html |
| 6 | EdChoy.com | Ed Choy | 5/5 | 2014-07-30 | "JR writes with the authority of one who has lived out missional life and equipped others to do the same" | https://www.edchoy.com/books/creating-missional-culture-jr-woodward/ |

---

## Review Sentiment Analysis

| Book | Positive | Mixed/Critical | Overall |
|------|----------|----------------|---------|
| Creating a Missional Culture | Majority positive; praised for practical APEST framework | Some critics note praxis-over-theology lean, desire more exegetical grounding | Well-received in missional circles |
| The Church as Movement | Praised for practical tools and interactive format | TGC review critiqued sociology-over-Scripture approach | Strong practitioner reception; IVP Book of the Year |
| The Scandal of Leadership | Overwhelmingly positive; "timely" and "significant" | Noted as dense/technical at times | Highest-rated of the three; resonates with abuse-aware communities |

---

*Research conducted via WebSearch and WebFetch on 2026-04-12. Goodreads data and review content verified at time of search.*

| 1 | DMin Dissertation | Asbury Theological Seminary | Missional Leadership | "Creating a Missional Culture" cited in dissertations on missional leadership approaches (multiple Asbury DMin theses reference IVP Forge series) |
| 2 | DMin Dissertation | George Fox University | Becoming Missional | "Becoming Missional: Essential Characteristics Necessary in Transitioning the Church to Engage a Postmodern Culture" -- references missional culture literature |
| 3 | Academic Paper | Various | Missional Leadership Literature Review | "Missional Leadership: A Critical Review of the Research Literature" (ResearchGate) -- systematic review of peer-reviewed articles and dissertations on missional leadership |
| 4 | Academic Paper | Various | Making Disciples on Mission | "Making Disciples on Mission: An Old Task for a New Era" (Academia.edu) |
| 5 | Academic Paper | Various | Missional Church Growth | "Missional Church Growth: Towards A Synthetic Missiology in Western Context" (Academia.edu) |

**Note**: Google Scholar reports ~274 total citations across all works. The bulk of these are from DMin dissertations, missiology papers, and church-planting literature. Precise per-paper citation counts were not retrievable due to Scholar page rendering limitations.

### Books That Reference Woodward

Woodward's work is situated within and cited by the broader missional theology movement. Authors who are likely to cite his work based on their shared ecosystem:

| Author | Notable Work | Likely Citation |
|--------|-------------|----------------|
| Alan Hirsch | The Forgotten Ways; The Permanent Revolution; 5Q | References to polycentric/APEST leadership (Woodward developed Hirsch's framework practically) |
| David Fitch | Faithful Presence; The Church of Us vs. Them | Shared theological framework on powers and mission |
| Michael Frost | The Shaping of Things to Come; Incarnate | Fivefold ministry / missional culture overlap |
| Dan White Jr. | Co-author of The Church as Movement | Direct collaboration |
| Tim Catchim | The Permanent Revolution (with Hirsch) | APEST framework development |
| Lance Ford | The Missional Quest; Unleader | Shared V3/missional movement ecosystem |

---

## Academic Context & Influence

### Theoretical Contributions

Woodward's academic work makes distinct contributions in three areas:

1. **APEST/Polycentric Leadership**: Creating a Missional Culture is recognized as "one of the most thorough developments" (Dr. Carlus Gupton) of the Ephesians 4:11 fivefold ministry framework for practical congregational application.

2. **Theology of the Powers & Leadership Failure**: The Scandal of Leadership applies Walter Wink's powers theology, Rene Girard's mimetic theory, and William Stringfellow's framework to analyze church leadership abuse -- a unique interdisciplinary synthesis.

3. **Movement Ecclesiology**: The Church as Movement contributes to the practical literature on missional-incarnational community formation, bridging theory and praxis.

### PhD Research

| Detail | Value |
|--------|-------|
| Institution | University of Manchester |
| Focus | Theology of the Powers and its implications for missional leadership |
| Key Scholars Engaged | Walter Wink, Rene Girard, William Stringfellow |
| Published As | The Scandal of Leadership (100 Movements, 2023) |
| Affiliated Center | Manchester Wesley Research Centre (http://www.mwrc.ac.uk/jr-woodward) |

### Teaching Positions (Citation Multiplier)

Woodward's adjunct positions at multiple seminaries increase his citation footprint through student exposure:

| Institution | Role |
|-------------|------|
| Fuller Theological Seminary | Adjunct Professor |
| Central Seminary | Adjunct Professor |
| Missio Seminary | Adjunct Professor |
| America Evangelical University | Adjunct Professor |

## Recommendations for Further Research

1. **Google Scholar direct scrape**: The Scholar profile (user=Igz_vYAAAAAJ) contains full citation data but requires browser rendering. A manual visit would yield exact per-publication citation counts and h-index.
2. **ProQuest Dissertations & Theses**: Search for "Woodward" + "Creating a Missional Culture" to identify all doctoral dissertations citing this work.
3. **Semantic Scholar**: Cross-reference with https://www.semanticscholar.org for additional citation graph data.
4. **ATLA Religion Database**: Search for academic journal articles citing Woodward in theological periodicals.

### Reach Tier Assessment

| Tier | Range | Assessment |
|------|-------|-----------|
| Micro (< 10K combined) | | |

| Major (250K+) | | |

**Estimated tier**: Growing (10K-50K)

**Estimated total reach**: ~25,000-40,000 unique individuals across all channels

**Rationale**: Social media following (~22K combined Twitter + Facebook author page) provides the visible floor. The 1,000+ V3 church planters represent an intensely engaged core audience -- these are practitioners who completed multi-month training programs, not passive followers. His 650 Goodreads ratings suggest 6,500-13,000 total book readers (ratings typically represent 5-10% of readers for niche academic-practitioner titles). Seminary teaching across 4 institutions adds several hundred students per year who encounter his work. The 477 Academia.edu followers indicate meaningful academic penetration. Conference speaking at Exponential, Awakenings, and Missio Alliance events adds several thousand cumulative attendees. His audience is smaller than peers like Alan Hirsch but disproportionately practitioner-heavy -- these are church planters, missional community leaders, and seminary students who actively implement his frameworks, not passive content consumers.

---

## Audience Profile

### Who Is the Audience?

**Primary audience**: Church planters and missional community leaders actively starting or sustaining new faith communities in North America. Typically ages 28-45, seminary-educated or in training, often bi-vocational, connected through V3, Forge, Missio Alliance, or Exponential networks. They use Woodward's polycentric leadership framework and "four spaces of belonging" model as practical tools for community design.

**Secondary audience**: Senior pastors and denominational leaders questioning hierarchical leadership models and seeking alternatives after witnessing leadership scandals and burnout. Ages 35-55, established in ministry, drawn to Woodward through *The Scandal of Leadership* and podcast appearances on shows like Theology in the Raw and The Roys Report. They are looking for theological frameworks to diagnose power dysfunction in their organizations.

**Tertiary audience**: Seminary students and academic missiologists studying missional ecclesiology, powers and principalities theology, and movement theory. They encounter Woodward through assigned reading at Fuller, Central Seminary, Missio Seminary, or America Evangelical University, and through his Academia.edu profile and Google Scholar citations (~274). Also includes justice-oriented Christians who discovered his Substack "Faithful Resistance" through its intersection of theology and political analysis.

### Audience Demographics (Estimated)

| Dimension | Assessment |
|-----------|-----------|
| Primary role | Church planter / Missional community leader / Seminary student / Denominational strategist |
| Age range | 28-55 (core: 30-45) |
| Education | High -- majority have seminary education (MDiv, MA, DMin) or are currently in seminary programs |
| Denominational breadth | Broad but centrist-evangelical -- spans non-denominational, mainline Protestant, Anabaptist-influenced, and charismatic traditions. Evidence: Missio Alliance's "centrist evangelical" positioning; V3 trains across denominations; published by IVP (broad evangelical) and 100 Movements (movement-focused) |
| Geographic concentration | US-centric (primarily urban -- Los Angeles, Pacific Northwest, major metro areas) with emerging international reach (V3 training in Africa, Asia; PhD from UK) |
| Gender split | Estimated 60-70% male based on church planting demographics; Woodward's emphasis on polycentric (non-hierarchical) leadership and justice themes may attract a higher proportion of women than typical church planting networks |
| Political orientation | Center to center-left among evangelicals; the "Faithful Resistance" Substack explicitly engages political theology from a justice-oriented perspective, attracting readers comfortable with prophetic social critique |

---

## Audience Personas

### Persona 1: Carlos -- V3 Church Planting Cohort Member

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Role | Bi-vocational church planter launching a missional community in a gentrifying urban neighborhood |
| Age | 34 |
| Education | MDiv from Fuller Theological Seminary |
| Tradition | Non-denominational, Anabaptist-influenced |
| Discovery path | Encountered *Creating a Missional Culture* through a Forge reading list; applied to V3 cohort after attending Praxis Gathering |
| Primary format | V3 cohort training (8 months) + books as reference texts + Substack |
| Use case | Applying the polycentric leadership model and "four spaces of belonging" to structure his church plant from inception |
| Pain point | Feels the tension between missional ideals and financial sustainability as a bi-vocational planter; wants practical tools, not just theory |

**What Carlos values in Woodward**: The V3 training program provides structured, cohort-based formation -- not just a weekend conference. The polycentric leadership model gives him language for why his team should not default to a senior-pastor-CEO structure. *The Church as Movement* (IVP Book of the Year 2017) is a workbook he uses with his team.

**What Carlos struggles with**: The 8-month V3 cohort is a significant time commitment for a bi-vocational planter. He wishes for more digital resources (video courses, downloadable tools) between cohort meetings. He finds Woodward's academic depth valuable but sometimes wants a quicker "how-to" path.

---

### Persona 2: Rachel -- Denominational Leader Rethinking Power

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Role | Regional director for a mainline Protestant denomination overseeing 40+ congregations |
| Age | 47 |
| Education | DMin in Missional Leadership |
| Tradition | PCUSA (Presbyterian Church USA) |
| Discovery path | Heard Woodward on the Theology in the Raw podcast (#1149) discussing the leadership crisis; ordered *The Scandal of Leadership* that week |
| Primary format | Books first, then podcasts, then Substack |
| Use case | Seeking a theological framework for addressing power abuses and clergy misconduct in her region; needs language for her board |
| Pain point | Has watched multiple pastors in her region crash from burnout or scandal; knows the system is broken but needs a constructive alternative, not just critique |

**What Rachel values in Woodward**: *The Scandal of Leadership* (4.77/5 on Goodreads) provides the most rigorous theological diagnosis she has found for why church leadership keeps failing. The Walter Wink / Rene Girard framework gives her an intellectual foundation beyond "bad apples" explanations. The book's 418 pages reflect serious scholarship, which she needs to persuade credentialed colleagues.

**What Rachel struggles with**: The book is dense (418 pages of PhD-derived theology). She wishes for an executive summary or workshop format she could bring to a denominational retreat. She also wonders whether Woodward's polycentric alternative is practical at the scale of 40+ congregations.

---

### Persona 3: Marcus -- Seminary Student and Substack Reader

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Role | PhD student in Practical Theology; part-time youth ministry director |
| Age | 29 |
| Education | MA in Theology (in progress: PhD) |
| Tradition | Progressive evangelical, justice-oriented |
| Discovery path | Found Woodward's Academia.edu profile while researching Walter Wink and powers theology; subscribed to "Faithful Resistance" Substack |
| Primary format | Substack (primary), academic papers (Academia.edu), books |
| Use case | Citing Woodward's dissertation work on powers and principalities in his own academic research; engaging with the political theology of "Faithful Resistance" |
| Pain point | Feels caught between academic missiology (which can feel abstract) and activist communities (which can lack theological depth). Woodward bridges this gap. |

**What Marcus values in Woodward**: The "Faithful Resistance" Substack is unique -- a PhD-level missiologist writing substantive political theology on Substack at a bi-weekly pace. Posts like "Authoritarianism is a Spiritual Crisis" and "Naming and Unmasking the Powers" blend academic rigor with prophetic urgency. Woodward's Academia.edu profile (477 followers, 8 papers) provides citable academic material.

**What Marcus struggles with**: The Substack is relatively new (launched ~2025) with a modest subscriber base. He wishes Woodward engaged more on social media or had a podcast where these ideas could be discussed in conversation. He also wishes for more academic publications beyond the dissertation-turned-book.

### Positioning Summary

JR Woodward occupies a distinctive niche in the missional ecclesiology space:

- **Smaller than Hirsch** in raw reach (~25-40K vs. ~150-200K) but with a more cohesive, practitioner-dense audience
- **Stronger academic credentials** than most peers (PhD Manchester, 4 adjunct roles, 274 citations, active Academia.edu profile)
- **Highest-rated recent book** in this peer group (*Scandal of Leadership* at 4.77/5 -- exceptional for any non-fiction title)
- **Most politically engaged voice** through "Faithful Resistance" Substack -- differentiates from Hirsch's more framework-focused content
- **Training pipeline is the anchor**: V3's 1,000+ trained planters represent the most deeply engaged audience segment
- **Digital presence is the gap**: No hosted podcast, no YouTube channel, no Wikipedia page, modest social following relative to institutional influence

---

## Movemental Audience Implications

- **Content format priority**: Training programs and structured courses should be the anchor offering. Woodward's audience is formed through multi-month cohorts (V3 discernment, V3 cohort, V3 immersions), not weekend conferences or viral social content. A Movemental-hosted digital training pathway could extend V3's reach beyond the current cohort model. Books are the secondary anchor -- his titles have excellent ratings (4.25 avg; 4.77 for *Scandal*) and serve as entry points to deeper engagement.

- **Topic focus**: *The Scandal of Leadership* content should be the lead -- it addresses the most urgent felt need in his audience (power abuse in the church), has the highest engagement signal (4.77/5, podcast concentration), and intersects with a post-2024 cultural moment around institutional accountability. Polycentric leadership / Ephesians 4 equipping content follows as the constructive alternative. "Faithful Resistance" political theology is a growth area that differentiates Woodward from every other author in the Movemental stable.

- **Cross-pollination with Alan Hirsch**: This is the highest-value author pairing on the platform. Hirsch wrote forewords for two of Woodward's three books, published him through 100 Movements, and shares the APEST/Ephesians 4 framework. Hirsch provides the macro-framework (mDNA, APEST, movement theory); Woodward provides the diagnostic (what goes wrong with leadership) and the political-prophetic edge (Faithful Resistance). A "Hirsch + Woodward" content track on polycentric leadership could be a flagship offering. Dan White Jr. (co-author of *The Church as Movement*) is the natural third voice.

- **Growth opportunity**: The biggest growth opportunity is digital infrastructure. Woodward has no hosted podcast, no personal YouTube channel, no free online course, no centralized video library, and a modest Substack (~hundreds of subscribers on a ~1-year-old publication). His content is scattered across Seminary Now, V3, conference recordings, and 10+ third-party podcast feeds. Movemental could centralize this dispersed content and provide the digital platform his institutional influence warrants. A Movemental-produced podcast or interview series featuring Woodward would fill a major gap.

- **Academic audience is unique**: Woodward's 477 Academia.edu followers, 274 Google Scholar citations, and 4 seminary adjunct roles give him a credentialed academic audience that most Movemental authors cannot match (Hirsch excepted). This audience can be reached through academic content tracks, syllabus adoption programs, and institutional partnerships.

- **Monetization signal**: Moderate-Strong. Woodward's audience already pays for content: V3 cohort training fees (multi-month programs), seminary tuition at 4 institutions, book purchases, Substack paid tier ($10/month or $100/year), and Praxis Gathering conference registration. The audience is comprised of church planters and denominational leaders who invest in leadership development. However, the audience is smaller than Hirsch's and skews toward bi-vocational planters with tighter budgets -- pricing should reflect this. The V3 training model (cohort-based, relationship-intensive) suggests the audience values depth over breadth and would pay premium for high-touch digital formation, not just self-paced video content.

---

# Content Analysis: JR Woodward

**Status**: Complete
**Last updated**: 2026-04-12
**Skill**: `/author-content-analysis`

---

## Executive Summary

JR Woodward is a practitioner-scholar whose work moves along a single deepening trajectory: the Western church has absorbed worldly patterns of power that distort its leadership, cripple its mission, and produce an epidemic of fallen leaders -- and the remedy is a polycentric, kenotic, movement-oriented ecclesiology grounded in the imitation of Christ rather than the imitation of the Powers. His distinctive contribution is the **synthesis of continental philosophy (Girard, Wink, Stringfellow) with hands-on church planting praxis** -- a combination virtually no other voice in the missional-incarnational movement offers at this depth. Operating as the architect to Alan Hirsch's prophet, Woodward builds carefully named frameworks (Five Culture Creators, Four Spaces of Belonging, Three Contours of Leadership) that translate abstract theology into deployable training systems. His body of work progresses from practical culture-building (*Creating a Missional Culture*) to movement-catalyzing (*The Church as Movement*) to deep diagnostic theology (*The Scandal of Leadership*), each layer adding sophistication to the same fundamental vision: the church as a neighborhood-rooted, discipleship-fueled, boundary-crossing movement led by many centers rather than one.

---

## Theme Map

### Primary Themes (Core to their identity)

| Theme | Description | Key Works | Centrality |
|-------|-------------|-----------|------------|
| Polycentric Leadership | Leadership structured around "many centers that interrelate" rather than hierarchical (CEO-pastor) or flat (undifferentiated) models. Reflects Trinitarian theology -- God's own communal nature. | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012), Missio Alliance articles, Verge Network talks, V3 training curriculum | 10 |
| Theology of the Powers | A robust synthesis of Wink (powers embodied in systems), Girard (mimetic desire and scapegoating), and Stringfellow (Image, Institution, Ideology). Powers are created good but fallen and redeemable; Satan/demonic forces are emergent realities without redemptive possibility. | PhD thesis (2020), *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023), Substack "Faithful Resistance," Missio Alliance 3-part series | 10 |
| APEST as Culture Creators | Ephesians 4:11 gifts reframed as culture-shaping vocations: Dream Awakeners (apostles), Heart Revealers (prophets), Story Tellers (evangelists), Soul Healers (pastors), Light Givers (teachers). Each creates a distinct environment necessary for missional community. | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012), Five Equippers Vimeo series, Missio Alliance talks, V3 training | 9 |
| Mimetic Desire & Imitation | Drawing on Girard: desires are not self-generated but formed through models. Leaders who unconsciously absorb worldly power models reproduce domination regardless of stated theology. "Not to imitate Christ is to imitate the Powers." | PhD thesis (2020), *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023), Theology in the Raw interview, Faith in a Fresh Vibe 2-part interview | 9 |
| Church as Neighborhood-Rooted Movement | The church should be locally embedded, not institutionally detached. Movement ecclesiology over institutional maintenance. Eight competencies for creating movemental communities. | *The Church as Movement* (2016), V3 blog posts, Praxis Gathering, IVP Academic chapter "What Would God's Reign Look Like In Our Neighborhood?" | 9 |

### Secondary Themes (Recurring but not defining)

| Theme | Description | Key Works | Centrality |
|-------|-------------|-----------|------------|
| Kenotic Leadership | The alternative to domineering leadership is self-emptying (kenotic) spirituality that reshapes desires through the imitation of Christ. Oscar Romero as primary exemplar. | *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023), Substack posts on Oscar Romero, Faith in a Fresh Vibe Part 2 | 8 |
| Missional Culture Formation | Culture -- not strategy, vision, or programs -- is the unseen force that shapes a church's effectiveness. The Cultural Web (six interconnected dimensions: Language, Artifacts, Rituals, Ethics, Institutions, Guiding Narratives). | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012), V3 blog posts, Verge Network articles | 7 |
| Post-Christendom Ecclesiology | Christianity moved from "a fellowship in Palestine, a philosophy in Greece, an institution in Rome, a government in Europe, and an enterprise in America." The corporate-enterprise model must be dismantled. | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012), Missio Alliance articles, V3 blog, NLCF founding context | 7 |
| Identity Before Action | "Being" precedes "doing" in mission. God changes people by changing their identities before calling them to tasks. Hebraic methodology: identity before imperative, narrative before proposition. | All three books, Verge Network articles, V3 training philosophy | 7 |
| Discipleship in Four Spaces | A framework for understanding how discipleship and mission happen across four relational spaces of varying intimacy and size. | V3 blog posts, Pivot Podcast interview, V3 Immersion course (with Eun Strawser) | 6 |
| Five Cultural Megashifts | Five macro transitions missional leaders must navigate: Media (print/broadcast to digital), Philosophy (modernity to postmodernity), Science (classical to emergent), Geography (rural to urban), Religion (Christendom to post-Christendom). | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012) | 5 |

### Emerging Themes (Recent or developing)

| Theme | Description | Evidence | Direction |
|-------|-------------|----------|-----------|
| Faithful Resistance to Concentrated Power | How the Church can stand firm as technocrats, autocrats, and oligarchs remake the world. Applies Powers theology to contemporary political dynamics. | Substack "Faithful Resistance" (2025-2026), 21 posts including "Authoritarianism is a Spiritual Crisis," "Prophetic Discipleship: Love on Trial" series (16 parts) | Expanding -- most politically engaged writing of his career; represents a new application of his doctoral research to current events |
| Prophetic Discipleship | A 16-part series connecting the Beatitudes to faithful resistance: each Beatitude as a form of counter-imperial discipleship. | Substack series (2025-2026), 11 of 16 parts published | Deepening -- the most systematic articulation of his spirituality-meets-resistance framework |
| AI, Technology, and the Powers | How the Powers operate through technological systems; faithful witness in a world reshaped by AI and concentrated digital power. | Substack tagline and framing; "The Medium and the Mission" (Academia.edu paper) | Exploratory -- framing is present but full theological treatment not yet published |
| Nonviolent Resistance as Ecclesial Practice | Nonviolent resistance research (the "3.5% rule") applied to church faithfulness under authoritarian pressure. | "The Power of the 3.5%" Substack post (2025) | Emerging -- connecting political science research to ecclesiology |

---

## Named Frameworks & Models

| Framework | Source | Components | Type |
|-----------|--------|------------|------|
| **Polycentric Leadership** | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012) | Leadership as "many centers that interrelate" -- neither hierarchical (top-down) nor flat (undifferentiated). Reflects Trinitarian community. Activates priesthood of all believers. | Structural model |
| **Five Culture Creators** | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012) | Dream Awakener (apostle), Heart Revealer (prophet), Story Teller (evangelist), Soul Healer (pastor), Light Giver (teacher) -- each creates a distinct cultural environment | Role framework (Eph 4:11 reframing) |
| **Five Environments** | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012) | Learning, Healing, Welcoming, Liberating, Thriving -- each corresponds to one of the five culture creators | Cultural assessment model |
| **The Cultural Web** | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012) | Language, Artifacts, Rituals, Ethics, Institutions, Guiding Narratives -- six interconnected dimensions shaping congregational and neighborhood culture | Diagnostic framework |
| **Five Cultural Megashifts** | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012) | Media, Philosophy, Science, Geography, Religion -- five macro-level transitions missional leaders must navigate | Contextual analysis |
| **Eight Movement Competencies** | *The Church as Movement* (2016) | Movement Intelligence, Polycentric Leadership, Being Disciples, Making Disciples, Missional Theology, Ecclesial Architecture, Community Formation, Incarnational Practice | Training curriculum |
| **Four Spaces of Belonging** | V3 blog / training | Four relational spaces of varying intimacy and size for discipleship and mission | Relational-spatial model |
| **Theology of the Powers** | PhD thesis (2020), *Scandal of Leadership* (2023) | Principalities (created good, fallen, redeemable) vs. Satan/demonic (emergent, unredeemable). Powers operate through Image, Institution, Ideology (Stringfellow). Mimetic desire (Girard) as mechanism of capture. Scapegoating as systemic pattern. | Theological diagnostic |
| **Imitation-Based Leadership Framework** | PhD thesis (2020), *Scandal of Leadership* (2023) | Leaders are inescapably imitative (per Girard). Imitate worldly power models = domineering. Imitate Christ's kenosis = life-giving servant leadership. Binary choice: "Not to imitate Christ is to imitate the Powers." | Leadership formation model |
| **Three Contours of Leadership** | *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023) | Identity (who leaders are), Praxis (how they lead and relate), Telos (what they value and pursue). Domineering leaders malform across all three. | Diagnostic assessment |

---

## Intellectual Genealogy

### Upstream Influences (Who shaped them)

| Thinker | Influence Area | How |
|---------|---------------|-----|
| Walter Wink | Theology of the Powers | Naming, unmasking, and engaging principalities embodied in systems; the "Domination System" as a spiritual-structural reality. Foundation of Woodward's PhD research. |
| Rene Girard | Mimetic desire theory | Triangular desire (we desire what our models desire); scapegoat mechanism; Jesus as the one who reveals and disrupts scapegoating. Core theoretical engine of *The Scandal of Leadership*. |
| William Stringfellow | Prophetic resistance | Powers manifest through Image, Institution, and Ideology; the "power of resurrection" against the "power of death." Third pillar of Woodward's Powers theology. |
| Oscar Romero | Exemplar of kenotic leadership | Positive model of resisting the Powers through self-emptying service under persecution. Woodward's primary biographical case study. |
| Lesslie Newbigin | Post-Christendom missiology | The West as mission field; the church as "sign, foretaste, and instrument" of the Kingdom. Shared influence with Hirsch. |
| Alan Hirsch | Apostolic movement, APEST | The foundational APEST framework that Woodward extends and applies practically. Hirsch wrote forewords for two of Woodward's books. |
| James K.A. Smith | Cultural liturgies | Formation of desire through practices and habits. Referenced in *Creating a Missional Culture*. |
| Henri Nouwen | Spiritual formation | Pastoral identity and inner life. Cited in *Creating a Missional Culture*. |
| Miroslav Volf | Theology of embrace | Reconciliation and communal identity. Cited in *Creating a Missional Culture*. |

### Downstream Impact (Who they've shaped)

| Person/Movement | Connection | Evidence |
|----------------|-----------|----------|
| V3 church planters (1,000+) | Direct training through Praxis Community cohorts | V3 training page: 600+ planters over 10 years; goal of 600 more in next 5 |
| Missio Alliance network | Co-founder; shaped organizational theology | Missio Alliance grew from Ecclesia Network (also co-founded by Woodward) |
| Fuller DGL cohort students | Doctoral cohort leader | "Discovering Missional Paradigms for the Next Generation" (Spring 2025) |
| Seminary students (4 institutions) | Adjunct professor at Fuller, Central, Missio, America Evangelical | Teaching across multiple seminary contexts |
| Dan White Jr. | Co-author, co-leader | *The Church as Movement* (2016); White's *Subterranean* carries forward neighborhood-rooted ecclesiology |
| E.K. Strawser | Foreword writer for *Centering Discipleship* | Woodward's influence on next-generation discipleship thinkers |
| 100Movements / Movement Leaders Collective | Council member | Shaping the broader church-planting movement conversation |

### Intellectual Peers (Contemporary dialogue partners)

| Person | Relationship | Agreement/Tension |
|--------|-------------|------------------|
| Alan Hirsch | Closest senior collaborator; forewords for two books | Deep alignment on APEST/missional movement; Hirsch is more prophetic, Woodward more diagnostic-constructive. Hirsch provides overarching vision; Woodward provides practical-academic depth. |
| David Fitch | Fellow missional theologian; foreword for *Scandal of Leadership* | Shared framework on Powers and mission; both integrate continental philosophy with ecclesiology. Fitch more focused on political theology; Woodward more on leadership formation. |
| Dan White Jr. | Co-author, co-leader of V3 | Deep alignment; White brings more neighborhood/place theology; Woodward brings more systematic frameworks. |
| Amos Yong | Pentecostal theologian; afterword for *Scandal of Leadership* | Cross-tradition dialogue on Powers and pneumatology; Yong brings Pentecostal/charismatic perspective to Woodward's Anabaptist-adjacent ecclesiology. |
| Preston Sprinkle | Extended podcast conversation | Shared concern about leadership failure; Sprinkle brings wider evangelical audience. |
| Brad Brisco | Peer in missional church planting | Both translate post-Christendom missiology for practitioners; Brisco works within SBC structures, Woodward across denominational lines. Brisco focuses on covocational ministry; Woodward on polycentric leadership. |
| Michael Frost | Endorser; shared missional-incarnational framework | Aligned on incarnational ecclesiology; Frost more provocative and international; Woodward more framework-heavy and North American. |

---

## Theological Positioning

| Dimension | Position | Evidence |
|-----------|---------|----------|
| Ecclesiology | Polycentric, movement-oriented. The church is a neighborhood-rooted movement, not an institution. Multiple interrelated leadership centers reflect Trinitarian community. | Entire body of work; V3 training philosophy; "a sign, foretaste, and instrument of God's kingdom" |
| Missiology | Incarnational-missional. Go and be, not come and see. Locally embedded, boundary-crossing. | *The Church as Movement*; Kairos LA church plants; V3 philosophy |
| Leadership | Polycentric over hierarchical or flat. APEST as culture creators, not just roles. Kenotic (self-emptying) rather than domineering. | *Creating a Missional Culture*; *The Scandal of Leadership*; PhD thesis |
| Hamartiology (sin/evil) | Powers theology: principalities are created good but fallen and redeemable. Satan/demonic are emergent realities without redemptive possibility. Leadership failure is a theological-systemic problem, not just a psychological one. | *The Scandal of Leadership*; PhD thesis; Missio Alliance 3-part series |
| Anthropology | Humans are inescapably imitative beings (per Girard). Desires are socially formed, not self-generated. Identity precedes action. | *The Scandal of Leadership*; Substack; "God changes us by changing our identities" |
| Tradition | Post-Christendom, cross-denominational. Anabaptist-adjacent ecclesiology with Wesleyan-Methodist academic formation (PhD through Nazarene Theological College) and liberation theology motifs (Romero, Solis Foundation). | Denominational diversity of career; PhD institution; organizations co-founded |
| Praxis | Integrated practitioner-scholar. Always moves from diagnosis to framework to practical application. 30+ years of church planting grounds every theological claim. | V3 training; NLCF founding; Kairos LA; 7 organizations founded |
| Scope | Neighborhood to global. Primary focus on local incarnational presence, but V3 trains planters in Africa and Asia. | V3 international reach; Solis Foundation (Kenya); Fuller Global Mission Advisory Council |

---

## Content Evolution

### Timeline of Ideas

| Period | Focus | Key Work | Shift |
|--------|-------|----------|-------|
| 1989-2003 | Conventional church planting; Virginia Tech campus ministry | NLCF founding; Great Commission Ministries | Grassroots ministry experience; learning by doing |
| 2003-2012 | Missional culture building; polycentric leadership | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012); Kairos LA co-founding; move to Los Angeles | From campus ministry to urban incarnational church planting; develops Five Culture Creators, Cultural Web, Five Environments. Focus: "How do we make one church missional?" |
| 2012-2016 | Movement ecclesiology; multiplication competencies | *The Church as Movement* (2016, with Dan White Jr.); V3 founding; Forge America; Praxis Gathering; Missio Alliance | From single church culture to movement dynamics. Focus shifts from "how do we build one missional church?" to "how do we catalyze a movement of missional churches?" IVP Book of the Year 2017. |
| 2016-2023 | Power, desire, and imitation; deep diagnostic theology | PhD thesis at University of Manchester (2020); *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023) | Deepening into theological roots of leadership failure. Continental philosophy (Girard, Wink, Stringfellow) enters the framework. From constructive (what healthy leadership looks like) to diagnostic-prophetic (why leaders fall and what spiritual forces are at work). Most theologically sophisticated phase. |
| 2025-present | Faithful resistance; prophetic discipleship | Substack "Faithful Resistance"; Fuller DGL cohort; Wartburg Watch feature; Roys Report interview | Powers theology applied to contemporary political dynamics. Most politically engaged phase. "Prophetic Discipleship: Love on Trial" (16-part Beatitudes series) represents the integration of spirituality, resistance, and missional identity. |

### Has their thinking shifted?

Woodward's thinking has not shifted so much as deepened in concentric layers. His core commitment -- neighborhood-rooted, incarnational, movement-oriented ecclesiology -- has remained constant since the NLCF founding in 1989 and the move to Los Angeles in 2003. What has evolved is the diagnostic depth and philosophical sophistication applied to the same fundamental vision.

The most significant intellectual development is the turn toward mimetic theory and Powers theology during his PhD research (2016-2020). This added a dimension absent from his earlier work: a diagnostic framework for *why* churches default to domineering leadership, not just *what* healthy leadership looks like. The earlier work was constructive-practical (build this); the later work is diagnostic-prophetic (understand this before you build).

The 2025 Substack represents a further extension: applying the Powers framework to contemporary political dynamics (authoritarianism, concentrated tech power, oligarchy). This is his most publicly engaged writing and suggests the next phase may involve Woodward as a prophetic public intellectual, not just an ecclesiological trainer.

---

## Unique Contribution

### What only this author says

- **The Girard-Wink-Stringfellow synthesis applied to church leadership**: Woodward is the only voice in the missional-incarnational movement who has synthesized Girard's mimetic theory, Wink's Powers trilogy, and Stringfellow's prophetic resistance into a single diagnostic framework for understanding leadership failure in the church. Others cite one or two of these thinkers; Woodward integrates all three at PhD level and applies them practically.

- **"Not to imitate Christ is to imitate the Powers"**: This binary formulation -- that leaders face an inescapable either/or between imitating Christ's kenosis and unconsciously replicating the Powers' domination -- is Woodward's signature thesis. No other author in this space has framed the leadership crisis in these terms.

- **APEST as culture creators, not just roles**: While Hirsch developed the APEST framework, Woodward extended it into a culture-shaping model. The renaming (apostles as Dream Awakeners, prophets as Heart Revealers, etc.) and the mapping of each gift to a specific cultural environment (learning, healing, welcoming, liberating, thriving) is Woodward's original contribution. Dr. Carlus Gupton called it "one of the most thorough developments" of the Ephesians 4:11 framework.

- **The Cultural Web as ecclesiological tool**: Woodward's six-dimension cultural web (Language, Artifacts, Rituals, Ethics, Institutions, Guiding Narratives) applied to congregational culture is a unique diagnostic tool not found in other missional ecclesiology literature.

- **Domineering leadership as a theological problem**: Where others diagnose leadership failure through psychology, management theory, or moral categories, Woodward insists it requires a theology of the Powers. The systemic, spiritual, and mimetic forces that shape leadership desire cannot be addressed by better accountability structures alone.

### Where they disagree with peers

| Topic | Woodward's Position | Mainstream/Peer Position |
|-------|-------------------|------------------------|
| Root cause of leadership failure | Theological-systemic: mimetic desire + Powers of domination operating through institutional systems | Psychological-moral: individual character deficiency, lack of accountability, or burnout |
| How to fix toxic leadership | Kenotic spiritual formation that reshapes desires through the imitation of Christ; systemic dismantling of domination structures | Better governance, accountability structures, psychological screening, and mentoring |
| Flat vs. hierarchical leadership | Neither -- polycentric leadership as a third way. Multiple interrelated centers, not undifferentiated flatness or top-down hierarchy | Most reformers default to either stronger hierarchy (governance) or flatter structures (shared leadership). The "polycentric" category is Woodward's distinctive alternative. |
| APEST framework application | Each gift creates a distinct cultural environment; all five are needed to cultivate a full missional culture | APEST is primarily about identifying leadership roles and filling gaps on a team (Hirsch's more common application) |
| Source of desire | Desires are socially formed through mimetic models (Girard); leaders must consciously choose their models | Desires are largely internal; leadership formation focuses on character, skill, and calling |
| Church and powers of domination | The church itself can become a vehicle for the Powers when it adopts corporate structures and worldly power models | The church is generally seen as a force against darkness; internal corruption is treated as deviation rather than systemic capture |

### What would be lost without their work

Without Woodward's work, the missional-incarnational movement would lack its deepest diagnostic framework for understanding why churches default to domination despite good intentions. The Girard-Wink-Stringfellow synthesis applied to ecclesiology would remain in academic journals rather than reaching church planters through V3 training. The APEST framework would remain primarily a role-identification tool rather than a culture-shaping model. And the emerging conversation about faithful resistance to concentrated power (technological, political, economic) would lack a theologian who connects it to both historic Powers theology and practical missional praxis.

---

## Content Interconnections

### How themes connect across works

Woodward's body of work follows a clear deepening progression: **culture** (what shapes a church) leads to **movement** (how churches multiply) leads to **power** (what distorts both).

- *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012) provides the foundational framework -- polycentric leadership, five culture creators, the cultural web. This is the constructive vision: what a healthy missional community looks like from the inside.
- *The Church as Movement* (2016, with Dan White Jr.) expands the frame from one community to a movement of communities. Eight competencies for multiplication. The shift is from culture to catalysis.
- *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023) diagnoses what goes wrong. Why do churches that aspire to the vision of the first two books end up reproducing domination? The Powers theology provides the answer: mimetic desire captures leaders unconsciously, and institutional systems embody fallen principalities.
- *Faithful Resistance* (Substack, 2025-present) extends the diagnosis to the broader cultural moment. If Powers operate through institutional systems, what happens when political, technological, and economic powers converge toward authoritarianism?

Each work builds on and presupposes the previous. The early work is constructive; the later work is diagnostic. Together they form a complete arc: vision, multiplication, diagnosis, resistance.

### Recommended reading order

| Order | Work | Why this sequence |
|-------|------|------------------|
| 1 | *Creating a Missional Culture* (2012) | Foundational frameworks: polycentric leadership, five culture creators, cultural web. Most accessible entry point. |
| 2 | *The Church as Movement* (2016) | Expands from one community to a movement. Interactive format with exercises. Best read after understanding the cultural framework. |
| 3 | *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023) | The diagnostic layer. Best appreciated after understanding what Woodward is trying to protect (the vision of books 1-2). Dense but essential. |
| 4 | Substack "Faithful Resistance" (2025-present) | The contemporary application. Extends Powers theology to current political dynamics. Best read after the theological grounding of book 3. |
| 5 | PhD thesis / Academia.edu papers | For those wanting the full academic treatment behind *The Scandal of Leadership*. |

---

## Movemental Content Strategy Implications

- **Pillar mapping**: Woodward serves the **Missional Leadership**, **Movement Ecclesiology**, **Power & Institutional Critique**, and **Discipleship Formation** content pillars. His work also feeds into **Church Planting**, **Spiritual Formation**, and **Cultural Analysis** categories.

- **Cross-author connections**: Strong alignment with **Alan Hirsch** (APEST, apostolic movement -- Hirsch is the direct upstream influence; Woodward extends and applies Hirsch's frameworks). Natural pairing with **Dan White Jr.** (co-author), **David Fitch** (Powers theology, mission), **Brad Brisco** (missional church planting, post-Christendom). Conceptual overlap with **Michael Frost** (incarnational theology). Potential contrast/complement with authors representing more institutional or attractional ecclesiology.

- **Content gaps Movemental can fill**: (1) No audiobooks for any of his 3 authored books -- significant production opportunity; (2) No centralized video presence -- his 25-40 scattered videos could be aggregated and supplemented; (3) No online course on any discoverable platform despite running V3 training for 10+ years; (4) The Girard-Wink-Stringfellow synthesis is his most distinctive intellectual contribution but exists only in a 418-page book -- needs shorter-form expression; (5) The "Five Culture Creators" framework has strong assessment/diagnostic potential (like Hirsch's APEST assessment) but no digital tool exists.

- **Series potential**: (1) "Five Culture Creators" -- each equipper as a standalone lesson/article/video; (2) "Unmasking the Powers" -- a course translating the *Scandal of Leadership* thesis into accessible modules; (3) "Polycentric Leadership" -- practical guide to shared leadership models; (4) "Prophetic Discipleship" -- the Substack Beatitudes series repackaged as a formation course; (5) "Church as Movement" -- the eight competencies as an online cohort curriculum; (6) "Faithful Resistance" -- Powers theology applied to contemporary culture.

- **Searchable concepts**: polycentric leadership, missional culture, five equippers, APEST leadership, powers and principalities, mimetic desire, kenotic leadership, church as movement, missional community, dream awakener, domineering leadership, theology of the powers, Walter Wink church, Rene Girard leadership, scapegoating, self-emptying leadership, neighborhood church planting, four spaces of belonging, missional-incarnational, post-Christendom ecclesiology, faithful resistance, prophetic discipleship.

- **Distinctive positioning for Movemental**: Woodward's unique value is the **scholar-practitioner bridge at the deepest level** -- integrating continental philosophy with 30+ years of church planting. No other author in the missional movement offers both PhD-level Girardian analysis and street-level V3 church planting experience. This combination positions him as the go-to voice for leaders who want to understand *why* churches default to domination, not just *how* to build better ones.

# Content Analysis: JR Woodward

**Research Date**: January 4, 2026  
**Confidence Level**: High

## Content Thematic Analysis

### Primary Themes

Based on published books and professional roles, JR Woodward's content focuses on:

1. **Missional Culture**
   - Creating missional culture in churches
   - Establishing communities with missional DNA
   - Focus: "Creating a Missional Culture" (2012)

2. **Church as Movement**
   - Understanding church as movement rather than institution
   - Movement dynamics and multiplication
   - Focus: "The Church as Movement" (2016, co-authored)

3. **Leadership and Power Dynamics**
   - Unmasking powers of domination in the church
   - Leadership structures and practices
   - Focus: "The Scandal of Leadership" (2023, based on Ph.D. research)

4. **Church Planting**
   - 30+ years of practical church planting experience
   - Training church planters across North America
   - National Director of V3 Church Planting Movement

5. **Community Formation**
   - Tight-knit community development
   - Life-forming discipleship
   - Locally-rooted presence

6. **Boundary-Crossing Mission**
   - Mission that crosses boundaries
   - Missional theology and practice
   - Co-founder of Missio Alliance

7. **Discipleship**
   - Life-forming discipleship practices
   - Discipleship in missional context

8. **Missional Theology**
   - Academic and practical missional theology
   - Integration of theory and practice
   - Ph.D. research in missional leadership

### Theological Focus Areas

- **Missional Theology**: Core focus on missional church and movement
- **Ecclesiology**: Understanding of church as movement
- **Leadership Theology**: Power dynamics and leadership structures
- **Practical Theology**: Integration of theology and practice
- **Church Planting Theology**: Theological foundations for church planting

### Movement Focus

- **Church Planting Movements**: National Director of V3 Church Planting Movement
- **Missional Movements**: Co-founder of Missio Alliance
- **Movement Practice**: Co-founder of Praxis Gathering
- **Movement Training**: Training church planters across North America

### Recurring Topics and Subjects

- Missional culture creation
- Church as movement
- Leadership and power
- Church planting
- Community formation
- Discipleship
- Boundary-crossing mission
- Integration of theory and practice
- Training and equipping leaders

# Gap Analysis: JR Woodward

**Status**: Complete
**Last updated**: 2026-04-12
**Skill**: `/author-gap-analysis`
**Research completeness**: 13/13 phases complete

---

## Executive Summary

JR Woodward is a deeply credentialed practitioner-scholar (PhD Manchester, 3 authored books, 7 organizations founded/co-founded, 1,000+ church planters trained through V3, adjunct professor at 4 seminaries, 8 board roles) whose digital presence significantly under-represents his embodied expertise. His content is fragmented across 12+ organizational platforms he does not own, he has no personal YouTube channel, no audiobooks, no online course on any discoverable platform, no hosted podcast, and a personal website that underperforms his stature. The single biggest structural gap is **format poverty** -- despite a rich corpus of conference talks, seminary teaching, V3 training cohorts, and 30+ years of church planting wisdom, almost none of this has been repurposed into scalable digital formats. The second is **fragmentation** -- his influence flows through V3, Missio Alliance, 100 Movements, Forge, Fuller, Substack, and scattered podcast appearances, with no centralized hub connecting them. His Substack "Faithful Resistance" (launched 2025) represents an emerging owned-audience strategy, but it serves a narrower political-prophetic niche rather than his full intellectual range.

---

## Embodied Work Indicators

| Indicator | Evidence | Digital Capture |
|-----------|----------|-----------------|
| 30+ years of church planting | NLCF founding (1989, Virginia Tech); Kairos LA co-founding (2003, Los Angeles) | Minimal -- no case studies, video documentation, or published stories from either church plant |
| 1,000+ church planters trained | V3 Movement: 600+ over 10 years; goal of 600 more in next 5 | Moderate -- V3 training page exists but curriculum content is gated behind cohort enrollment |
| 7 organizations founded/co-founded | NLCF, Kairos LA, The Unembraced, Solis Foundation, Ecclesia Network, Missio Alliance, Praxis Gathering | Low -- organizational websites exist but Woodward's founding stories are not documented |
| PhD (University of Manchester) | Dissertation: "Missional Leadership, Mimetic Desire and a Theology of the Powers" | High -- published as *The Scandal of Leadership* (2023). Full academic treatment accessible. |
| 4 seminary adjunct positions | Fuller, Central, Missio, America Evangelical University | None -- no syllabi, lecture recordings, or course content published |
| 8 board/council roles | Missio Alliance, Reliant Mission, Movement Leaders Collective, Fuller Global Mission Advisory, Fuller Church Initiatives, KINEO, Ecclesia Network, GCM | None -- advisory work is invisible digitally |
| Annual Praxis Gathering (300+) | Co-founded; co-directed | Minimal -- event exists but no recorded sessions found online |
| East Hollywood Neighborhood Council | Civic engagement in LA | None -- not documented or connected to his ecclesiological writing |
| International training (Africa, Asia) | V3 trains planters internationally | Minimal -- referenced but not documented with stories, videos, or testimonials |
| Solis Foundation (Kenya) | Micro-grants for businesses serving people in extreme poverty | None -- no digital footprint found for this work |

---

## Primary Gaps Identified

### Gap 1: No Audiobooks

| Dimension | Assessment |
|-----------|-----------|
| **What's missing** | None of Woodward's 3 authored books have confirmed audiobook editions |
| **Why it matters** | Audiobook consumption continues to grow (20%+ year-over-year); his core audience (church planters, seminary students, busy pastors) are prime audiobook consumers |
| **Priority** | Critical |
| **Estimated revenue** | $3K-$10K/year across 3 titles |
| **Action** | Produce audiobook for *The Scandal of Leadership* first (highest-rated, most current); then *Creating a Missional Culture* (most accessible, widest audience) |

### Gap 2: No Centralized Video Presence

| Dimension | Assessment |
|-----------|-----------|
| **What's missing** | 20-30 videos scattered across Vimeo, Verge Network, V3 Movement, Missio Alliance, Seminary Now, and others' YouTube channels. No personal YouTube channel. Five Equippers series (est. 6 videos) may be partially lost due to domain expiration. |
| **Why it matters** | YouTube is the second-largest search engine. His peers (Hirsch, Frost, Breen) have centralized video presences. Prospective church planters searching for "polycentric leadership" or "missional culture" cannot find Woodward on YouTube. |
| **Priority** | Critical |
| **Estimated audience gain** | 5K-15K subscribers within 2 years based on comparable channels |
| **Action** | Create YouTube channel; aggregate existing content with permission; record new "Five Culture Creators" and "Unmasking the Powers" series; clip Substack content into short-form |

### Gap 3: No Online Course on Discoverable Platforms

| Dimension | Assessment |
|-----------|-----------|
| **What's missing** | V3 training (Praxis Cohorts, Immersions) is gated behind enrollment and not discoverable via search. Seminary Now content is behind a paywall. No presence on Teachable, Thinkific, Udemy, Skillshare, or similar platforms. |
| **Why it matters** | V3 has trained 1,000+ planters but the curriculum is invisible to anyone not already connected to V3. The Eight Movement Competencies, Five Culture Creators, and Four Spaces of Belonging are fully developed curricula waiting to be scaled. |
| **Priority** | Critical |
| **Estimated revenue** | $10K-$40K/year (based on comparable missional theology courses) |
| **Action** | Package V3 Immersion courses for Movemental platform; create standalone "Five Culture Creators" and "Unmasking the Powers" courses; use *Scandal of Leadership* as textbook for a Powers theology course |

### Gap 4: No Hosted Podcast

| Dimension | Assessment |
|-----------|-----------|
| **What's missing** | Woodward does not host or co-host any podcast. 11+ guest appearances demonstrate strong audio teaching ability but he has no owned audio channel. |
| **Why it matters** | His voice -- warm, scholarly yet accessible, systematically organized -- is well-suited to long-form audio. A podcast would convert his Substack written audience into audio subscribers and provide a regular content vehicle for his emerging "Faithful Resistance" platform. |
| **Priority** | High |
| **Estimated audience gain** | 2K-8K regular listeners within 18 months |
| **Action** | Launch a Movemental-hosted podcast or interview series; alternatively, add audio to Substack posts (Substack supports audio natively) |

### Gap 5: Website Underperforms

| Dimension | Assessment |
|-----------|-----------|
| **What's missing** | jrwoodward.com is a basic WordPress/Astra site. No prominent newsletter CTA, no embedded video, no book showcase, no media kit, no speaking page, no email capture. Legacy domain fragmentation (jrwoodward.com, .net, .me, .blogspot) creates confusion. jrwoodward.net (original blog) has expired and may host compromised content. |
| **Why it matters** | The personal website is the hub that should connect all spokes (V3, Missio Alliance, Substack, books, speaking). Currently it connects nothing. Visitors land and bounce. |
| **Priority** | High |
| **Action** | Redesign as a modern author hub: book showcase, newsletter signup, embedded video, speaking page, media kit, links to all platforms. Consolidate domains. |

### Gap 6: No Wikipedia Page

| Dimension | Assessment |
|-----------|-----------|
| **What's missing** | Unlike Alan Hirsch, Woodward has no Wikipedia page |
| **Why it matters** | Wikipedia pages are the top Google Knowledge Panel source. They establish authority, improve discoverability, and serve as a canonical reference. Woodward meets notability criteria (PhD, 3 published books with IVP and 100 Movements, 7 founded organizations, 1,000+ planters trained, IVP Book of the Year). |
| **Priority** | High |
| **Action** | Draft and submit Wikipedia article with proper sourcing from published reviews, publisher pages, and institutional references |

### Gap 7: Substack Serves Narrow Niche

| Dimension | Assessment |
|-----------|-----------|
| **What's missing** | "Faithful Resistance" focuses on Powers theology applied to contemporary political dynamics. This is important but represents only one layer of Woodward's expertise. His constructive ecclesiology (polycentric leadership, Five Culture Creators, movement competencies) and his diagnostic work (mimetic desire, leadership formation) are not served by the Substack. |
| **Why it matters** | The Substack audience (hundreds of subscribers) is growing but self-selects for political-prophetic content. Church planters seeking practical training, seminary students seeking frameworks, and leaders seeking diagnostic tools are not finding Woodward through this channel. |
| **Priority** | Medium |
| **Action** | Either broaden Substack scope or create separate content channels (Movemental profile, YouTube, courses) for the constructive/diagnostic work. Cross-promote to build bridges between audiences. |

## Connection Gaps (Fragmentation Analysis)

| Platform A | Platform B | Connection Status |
|-----------|-----------|------------------|
| jrwoodward.com | Substack | Weak -- no prominent CTA on website driving to newsletter |
| jrwoodward.com | V3 Movement | Weak -- no visible link or integration |
| Substack | V3 Training | None -- separate audiences, no cross-promotion |
| V3 Training | Fuller DGL | None -- no visible connection despite same leader |
| Missio Alliance | Substack | Minimal -- separate content streams |
| Books (Amazon/IVP) | Any owned platform | None -- no CTA in books driving to website, newsletter, or courses |
| Podcast appearances | Any owned platform | None -- no consistent CTA or landing page for listeners |
| Academia.edu | jrwoodward.com | None -- academic and popular audiences are siloed |
| Facebook (@missionalculture) | Substack | Moderate -- occasional cross-posting |
| X (@dreamawakener) | Substack | Moderate -- occasional cross-posting |

**Assessment**: Woodward's digital presence functions as 10+ disconnected islands rather than an integrated archipelago. A church planter who discovers his V3 training has no pathway to his Substack. A Substack reader has no pathway to his V3 courses. A podcast listener has no landing page. A student at Fuller has no connection to his broader body of work. This fragmentation means each platform under-serves the audience and under-represents Woodward's full range.

---

## Embodied Work vs. Digital Expression

### Strong embodied work NOT captured digitally

1. **30+ years of church planting stories** -- NLCF (Virginia Tech), Kairos LA (Hollywood, West LA, South LA), and V3-planted churches across North America, Africa, and Asia. No case studies, testimonials, video documentation, or published stories from any of these plants.
2. **V3 training curriculum** -- The Eight Movement Competencies, the Praxis Community experience, the Immersion courses represent years of refined pedagogy. This content is gated behind cohort enrollment and invisible to anyone not already in the V3 pipeline.
3. **Seminary teaching (4 institutions)** -- Years of lectures at Fuller, Central, Missio, and America Evangelical have no digital footprint. No syllabi, recordings, or course content published.
4. **Praxis Gathering (annual, 300+ attendees)** -- An annual conference with curated practitioners sharing street-level content. No recordings found online.
5. **Board-level strategic influence** -- Woodward serves on 8 boards/councils including Reliant Mission (500+ missionaries), Movement Leaders Collective, and Fuller Global Mission Advisory Council. This strategic influence is entirely invisible digitally.
6. **Solis Foundation and The Unembraced** -- Two Kenya-focused organizations with no discoverable digital presence. Represents a whole dimension of Woodward's work (global justice, extreme poverty) that is completely undocumented.
7. **East Hollywood Neighborhood Council service** -- Civic engagement that embodies his theology of neighborhood-rooted mission but is never referenced in his published work.

### Digital content NOT connected to embodied work

1. **Substack "Faithful Resistance"** -- Strong writing but disconnected from V3 training pipeline. Political-prophetic content does not reference or connect to his church planting methodology.
2. **Scattered podcast interviews** -- 11+ episodes without a consistent CTA, landing page, or connection to any owned platform.
3. **Facebook @missionalculture** -- Social media identity ("missional culture") does not connect to his later Powers/resistance work.
4. **Legacy blog (jrwoodward.net)** -- Domain expired; content from 2007-2016 may be partially or fully lost. Represents a decade of writing that should be archived and migrated.

---

### Long-term (12+ months)

| # | Action | Effort | Impact |
|---|--------|--------|--------|
| 16 | Launch hosted podcast (or Movemental-produced interview series) | High | High -- fills the owned-audio gap |
| 17 | Build digital "Five Culture Creators" assessment tool (interactive, shareable results) | High | High -- creates viral discoverability similar to Hirsch's APEST test |
| 18 | Record one full V3 Praxis Community cohort cycle for digital distribution | High | High -- captures his signature training for global scale |
| 19 | Create "Faithful Resistance" course connecting Powers theology to practical community action | Medium | Medium -- monetizes Substack audience |
| 20 | Develop "Prophetic Discipleship" formation curriculum from Substack Beatitudes series | Medium | Medium -- turns emerging content into structured learning |

### What comparable authors do better

| Author | Advantage | How to Close Gap |
|--------|-----------|-----------------|
| Alan Hirsch | Comprehensive digital ecosystem (5Q courses, APEST assessment tool, multiple branded websites, YouTube presence, extensive book library) | Build Movemental profile as unified hub; develop Five Culture Creators assessment as Woodward's equivalent to APEST test; create centralized video presence |
| David Fitch | Active social media, strong Substack presence, consistent conference circuit with recorded sessions | Increase Woodward's content frequency; ensure conference talks are recorded; strengthen Substack cross-promotion |
| Mike Breen | 3DM created a comprehensive online learning platform with video courses, cohort training, and downloadable tools | Package V3 training for digital distribution; Woodward's content quality matches but delivery infrastructure lags |
| Michael Frost | Prolific author (15+ books), strong international brand, YouTube presence, cohesive speaking circuit | YouTube channel + international content distribution; Woodward's depth matches but visibility lags |
| Brad Brisco | Strong NAMB/denominational distribution network; free eBook as lead magnet | Woodward needs a comparable free resource to drive email capture; his frameworks are equally strong but less discoverable |

### What Woodward does better than peers

| Strength | Evidence | How to Amplify |
|----------|----------|---------------|
| Academic-philosophical depth | PhD-level Girard/Wink/Stringfellow synthesis; only voice in missional movement integrating continental philosophy at this level | Create courses that translate this depth into accessible modules; "Unmasking the Powers" as signature course |
| Practitioner credibility | 30+ years across Virginia Tech, LA, V3 national scope; 7 organizations founded; 1,000+ planters trained | Document and publish case studies; lead with practitioner stories in all content; numbers are compelling if made visible |
| Framework-naming ability | "Dream Awakeners," "Heart Revealers," "polycentric leadership" -- evocative renaming that makes abstract concepts sticky | Create visual assets for each framework; build shareable framework diagrams; develop assessment tools |
| Cross-denominational reach | Works with planters from multiple backgrounds; not bound to single tradition | Position as the non-tribal voice for missional leadership; this breadth is rare and valuable |
| Emerging prophetic voice | Substack "Faithful Resistance" represents a timely, growing platform addressing concentrated power | Amplify through audio, video, and cross-platform distribution; this content is hitting at exactly the right cultural moment |
| Book review quality | 4.77/5 Goodreads rating for *Scandal of Leadership* (73 ratings, 46 reviews) is exceptional | Feature social proof prominently; use review quotes in all marketing; this rating signals deep audience resonance |

# Movemental Platform Fit: JR Woodward

**Status**: Complete

**Skill**: `/author-gap-analysis`
