## Fit Score

| Dimension | Score (1-10) | Notes |
|-----------|-------------|-------|
| Content volume | 7 | 4 books (3 authored, 1 edited), 8+ academic papers, 5+ immersion courses, 7+ podcast guest appearances, contributor articles across 6+ outlets (Missio Alliance, Verge Network, V3 blog, EMQ, Leadership Journal, Religious Studies Review). Less raw volume than some peers but substantial when V3 training materials are included. |
| Content quality | 9 | PhD from University of Manchester published as a book. IVP Book of the Year 2017. Goodreads average 4.25/5 across 650 ratings. *The Scandal of Leadership* at 4.77/5 is exceptional. Endorsed by Alan Hirsch, Michael Frost, David Fitch, Darrell Guder. ~274 Google Scholar citations. Academic rigor combined with practitioner credibility is rare. |
| Audience alignment | 9 | His audience (church planters, missional practitioners, seminary students, movement leaders, abuse-aware communities) maps directly to Movemental's core target. V3 has trained 1,000+ church planters. His Substack audience (justice-oriented, politically engaged Christians) adds a secondary audience that expands Movemental's reach beyond the traditional church planting niche. |
| Platform need | 8 | Digital Presence Score of 3.3/5. No centralized video presence, no hosted podcast, basic WordPress site, no lead magnet, no email funnel from website to Substack, domain fragmentation across 4 URLs, no Wikipedia page. He has substantial content scattered across Seminary Now, V3, conference channels, and third-party podcasts that needs a unified home. Slightly less urgent than some peers because his Substack is already a functioning content channel. |
| Network effects | 9 | Co-founder of Missio Alliance (connects to David Fitch, Deb Hirsch, MaryKate Morse, Leroy Barber, Jo Anne Lyon). National Director of V3 (1,000+ trained planters). Published through Alan Hirsch's 100Movements. Council member of Movement Leaders Collective. Board member of Reliant Mission (500+ missionaries), Fuller Global Mission Advisory Council, KINEO. 7 organizations founded/co-founded, 8 board roles. One of the most connected figures in the missional movement. |
| Digital maturity | 4 | Active Substack with paid tier shows digital intent. Clean handle consistency (@dreamawakener). But website is WordPress/Astra (basic), no YouTube channel, Instagram dormant, no course platform beyond V3's organizational site, no analytics infrastructure, no lead magnets, no email capture on main site. Comfortable creating digital content but not digitally strategic. |
| Growth potential | 8 | Significant runway: V3 training content not digitized for wider distribution, 30-week Praxis Cohort curriculum has no public-facing course equivalent, PhD research provides years of Substack and article content, Fuller DGL cohort leadership creates ongoing pipeline, the "Faithful Resistance" Substack niche (theology + political engagement) is growing. His audience of abuse-aware communities is expanding as church accountability conversations intensify. |
| **Overall Fit** | **7.7/10** | |

---

## What Movemental Would Change for This Author

### Problems Movemental Solves

- **Platform fragmentation**: His content lives across 12+ platforms he doesn't own (V3 site, Seminary Now, Missio Alliance, Verge Network, Academia.edu, Amazon, Goodreads, IVP, 100Movements, multiple podcast hosts, conference archives, WordPress blog). Movemental provides a single owned hub with structured navigation.
- **No audience ownership beyond Substack**: He reaches thousands through V3 training, conference speaking, and institutional channels, but his only owned audience channel is a Substack with "hundreds" of subscribers. No email capture on his main website. No way to communicate directly with the 1,000+ church planters V3 has trained outside of organizational channels.
- **Invisible training archive**: 30+ weeks of Praxis Cohort curriculum, 4-6 week immersion courses, 12-week Reimagining Church program, Fuller DGL cohort content, and 4 seminary teaching positions generate zero publicly accessible digital content. This represents the largest untapped content reservoir.
- **Video content scattered**: Teaching content exists across Seminary Now, V3 media, Exponential recordings, Awakenings Gathering recordings, and third-party podcast video channels. No centralized personal video presence or YouTube channel.
- **No monetization infrastructure beyond books and Substack**: Amazon royalties, IVP/100Movements royalties, and Substack's optional $10/month tier are his only direct content revenue streams. No course platform, no downloadable resources, no community membership offering.
- **Domain and brand fragmentation**: jrwoodward.com, jrwoodward.net, jrwoodward.me, and a legacy Blogspot all create confusion. The personal website (WordPress/Astra) underperforms for an author of his stature -- no book showcase, no embedded media, no newsletter CTA.
- **Academic content locked in silos**: 477 Academia.edu followers, 8 papers, and ~274 Google Scholar citations represent significant scholarly credibility that is invisible to his practitioner audience. His PhD thesis-to-book pipeline (University of Manchester -> *The Scandal of Leadership*) is a model others would learn from, but nowhere is this journey made accessible.

### Content Movemental Would Surface

- **4 books** -- cataloged with summaries, key frameworks, purchase links, review excerpts, and cross-references to related courses/articles in a unified author profile
- **8+ academic papers** from Academia.edu -- organized by theme (digital culture and missiology, leadership, election doctrine, development) with accessible summaries for non-academic readers
- **7+ podcast guest appearances** -- indexed with topic tags, timestamps, and links to related written content
- **25+ contributor articles** from 6+ platforms (Missio Alliance, Verge Network, V3 blog, EMQ, Leadership Journal, Religious Studies Review, Gospel Centered Discipleship, newchurches.com) -- aggregated by theme
- **V3 training overview** -- structured description of the Praxis Community Cohort pathway, immersion courses, and Reimagining Church program, presented as a learning pathway
- **Network map** -- his relationships with Alan Hirsch, Dan White Jr., David Fitch, Michael Frost, and 8+ board positions visualized as a collaborative ecosystem
- **Key frameworks** -- the Five Equippers, Eight Core Competencies, Four Spaces of Belonging, and Theology of the Powers presented as interactive, cross-referenced learning tools

### New Content Movemental Would Enable

- **Online courses**: Digitized versions of V3 immersion courses ("Starting a Movement," "The Craft of Discipleship," "Created for Connection & Mission"), adapted from the 4-6 week cohort format to self-paced modules. A "Theology of the Powers" course drawn from *The Scandal of Leadership* and his PhD research. A "Polycentric Leadership" course drawn from *Creating a Missional Culture*.
- **Email newsletter integration**: Bridge between Substack "Faithful Resistance" and Movemental profile, with cross-promotion and email capture on the Movemental author page.
- **Video content**: Centralized video library consolidating Seminary Now sessions, V3 media, and conference recordings. New short-form video teachings (2-3 minutes) from his key frameworks, optimized for social sharing.
- **Downloadable resources**: Five Equippers assessment tool, Eight Core Competencies self-evaluation, Missional Culture diagnostic, "Theology of the Powers" study guide, Praxis Cohort orientation materials.
- **Community features**: Discussion spaces for V3 alumni, course cohorts, and Faithful Resistance readers. A structured community that bridges his training, writing, and newsletter audiences.
- **Audiobook editions**: Production pipeline for *The Scandal of Leadership* (418 pages) and *Creating a Missional Culture* (224 pages) -- neither has a confirmed audiobook.

---

## Onboarding Recommendations

### Phase 1: Quick Wins (Week 1)

1. **Create Movemental author profile** with bio, headshot, and links to all existing books, platforms, and organizational roles
2. **Import article catalog** -- aggregate contributor articles from Missio Alliance, Verge Network, V3 blog, EMQ, Leadership Journal, and other outlets with theme tagging
3. **Index podcast appearances** -- create searchable catalog of 7+ guest episodes with topic descriptions and timestamps
4. **Set up book listings** -- all 4 books with covers, descriptions, purchase links, Goodreads ratings, review excerpts, and related content cross-references
5. **Create framework pages** -- standalone pages for the Five Equippers, Eight Core Competencies, Four Spaces of Belonging, and Theology of the Powers with visual diagrams
6. **Claim key URLs** -- reserve jrwoodward.movemental.com (or equivalent)

### Phase 2: Content Migration (Month 1)

1. **Launch newsletter bridge** -- connect Substack "Faithful Resistance" to Movemental profile with cross-links, archive page, and email capture CTA on the author profile page
2. **Consolidate video content** -- gather Seminary Now sessions, V3 media recordings, Exponential conference talks, and podcast video appearances into a unified, tagged video library on Movemental
3. **Create "Theology of the Powers" content hub** -- a pillar page aggregating *The Scandal of Leadership*, related Substack posts, academic papers, and podcast appearances on this theme
4. **Create "Missional Culture" content hub** -- a pillar page aggregating *Creating a Missional Culture*, related articles, the Five Equippers framework, and endorsement context
5. **Surface academic profile** -- integrate Academia.edu papers, Google Scholar citations, and PhD research narrative into a "Research" section of the author profile

### Phase 3: Content Creation (Month 2-3)

1. **Record first online course** -- "The Scandal of Leadership: Understanding Power in the Church" drawn from his PhD research, book, and Substack content. 6-8 sessions covering Wink, Girard, Stringfellow, the Powers framework, and Christlike alternatives.
2. **Produce audiobook** -- *The Scandal of Leadership* (418 pages, highest-rated book) narrated by Woodward or a professional narrator
3. **Create downloadable toolkit** -- "Five Equippers Assessment" extracted from *Creating a Missional Culture* as a practical team diagnostic tool
4. **Develop visual frameworks** -- shareable graphics for Five Equippers, Eight Core Competencies, Four Spaces of Belonging, Image-Institution-Ideology diagnostic
5. **Record 5-10 short-form videos** -- 2-3 minute teachings on core topics (What is polycentric leadership? What are the Powers? Why imitation matters. The Four Spaces.) optimized for social sharing

### Phase 4: Growth (Ongoing)

1. **Newsletter growth** -- target 2,000 subscribers within 12 months using Movemental profile, podcast appearances, and V3 network as promotion channels. Every guest appearance = newsletter CTA.
2. **Course expansion** -- add "Creating a Missional Culture" course (from book + V3 immersion content) and "The Church as Movement" course (from book + Praxis Cohort frameworks)
3. **Collaborative content** -- co-create a course or content series with Dan White Jr. leveraging their *Church as Movement* co-authorship and V3 partnership
4. **V3 alumni community** -- build a Movemental-hosted community for the 1,000+ church planters V3 has trained, creating an alumni network that extends the training relationship
5. **YouTube channel** -- establish personal channel, begin uploading clipped conference talks, short-form teachings, and Substack audio versions. Target 1,000 subscribers in year 1.
6. **SEO strategy** -- build content clusters around "missional culture," "polycentric leadership," "theology of the powers," and "church planting movement" with Movemental profile as hub
7. **Wikipedia page** -- support creation of a Wikipedia article (PhD, IVP Book of the Year, 7 organizations, ~274 citations provide notability) to close the discoverability gap vs. peers like Alan Hirsch

---

## What We Will NOT Do

- **Replace V3 Movement**: Movemental is complementary to V3's training infrastructure, not competitive. V3's Praxis Cohorts, immersion courses, and coaching model continue unchanged. Movemental amplifies JR's personal voice and extends V3's reach, but does not replace the relational, cohort-based training model.
- **Remove content from existing platforms**: Articles on Missio Alliance, Verge Network, V3 blog, and other outlets stay where they are. Academic papers remain on Academia.edu. Movemental aggregates and links; it does not extract.
- **Compete with Substack**: "Faithful Resistance" is a distinct publication with its own voice (more politically engaged than his books). Movemental complements the Substack by providing the broader professional profile, course infrastructure, and community tools that Substack does not offer. The Substack remains the primary newsletter channel.
- **Dilute the academic voice**: His PhD research and scholarly credibility are core differentiators. Movemental will surface this work accessibly but will not dumb it down or strip the academic rigor from his content.
- **Change his theological positions**: His missional theology (Newbigin-influenced, incarnational, kenotic, justice-oriented) is preserved exactly as is. His Substack's political engagement ("Faithful Resistance") is his voice -- Movemental doesn't edit, soften, or reframe.
- **Force social media activity**: If he prefers Twitter/X and Substack as his primary channels, that's fine. Movemental enhances what exists rather than demanding Instagram Reels or TikTok content.
- **Pressure monetization**: Some of his best content (V3 training frameworks, academic papers, Substack posts) is free and accessible. Movemental provides monetization tools but doesn't require their use.

## What Remains the Same

- **His voice**: The practitioner-scholar tone that moves between academic rigor and grounded practical wisdom -- from Girard and Wink to neighborhood church planting stories
- **His theology**: Missional-incarnational, kenotic leadership, theology of the Powers, polycentric leadership, APEST-informed ecclesiology -- the coherent framework developed over 30+ years
- **His relationships**: The collaborative partnerships with Dan White Jr., Alan Hirsch, David Fitch, Jesse Eubanks, and the broader Missio Alliance / 100Movements ecosystem
- **His V3 role**: National Director of V3 Church Planting Movement continues as his primary vocational context
- **His books**: All 4 titles continue to be published and sold through existing channels (IVP, 100Movements Publishing, Amazon)
- **His Substack**: "Faithful Resistance" continues as his primary newsletter and long-form content channel
- **His academic positions**: Adjunct appointments at Fuller, Central Seminary, Missio Seminary, and American Evangelical University continue independently
- **His board service**: All 8 board/council roles (Missio Alliance, Reliant Mission, Fuller, KINEO, Movement Leaders Collective, etc.) continue unchanged
- **His conference speaking**: Praxis Gathering, Awakenings, Exponential, and other speaking engagements continue independently
- **His Washington DC presence**: Local involvement with District Church and the DC-area community remains his embodied context

**Organizational Platforms**:
- Content tied to organizations, not personal brand
- Limited personal control over organizational platforms
- Content may not be easily portable

**Academic Platforms**:
- Academic content separate from practical content
- Limited integration with practical platforms
- Academic audience separate from practitioner audience

**Publisher Platforms**:
- Books tied to publisher platforms
- Limited control over book presentation and marketing
- Books may not be easily connected to other content

## Movemental Fit Analysis

### Gaps Movemental Specifically Addresses

**1. Platform Unification**:
- **Current State**: Content scattered across multiple platforms (personal website, organizational platforms, academic platforms, publisher platforms)
- **Movemental Solution**: Unified platform for all content
- **Impact**: All content in one place, easier discovery and connection

**2. Content Interconnection**:
- **Current State**: Content potentially isolated across platforms (to be verified)
- **Movemental Solution**: Built-in content interconnection and cross-referencing
- **Impact**: Books, articles, courses, videos all connected in one ecosystem

**3. Content Repurposing**:
- **Current State**: Limited content repurposing (books standalone, teaching not expanded) (to be verified)
- **Movemental Solution**: Easy content repurposing across forms (articles, courses, videos, podcasts)
- **Impact**: Teaching, training, books can be expanded into multiple content forms

**4. Series Development**:
- **Current State**: Books standalone, limited series development (to be verified)
- **Movemental Solution**: Built-in series development tools
- **Impact**: Books can become article series, courses, video series

**5. Discoverability**:
- **Current State**: Content discoverability limited by platform fragmentation (to be verified)
- **Movemental Solution**: Unified platform with network effects and SEO optimization
- **Impact**: Content more discoverable through network and platform optimization

**6. Revenue Model**:
- **Current State**: Revenue through publishers and organizations, limited direct revenue (to be verified)
- **Movemental Solution**: Built-in subscription, course, and book revenue models
- **Impact**: Direct revenue from content, not dependent on publishers/organizations

**7. Analytics**:
- **Current State**: Analytics across multiple platforms, no unified view (to be verified)
- **Movemental Solution**: Unified analytics across all content
- **Impact**: Better insight into content performance and audience engagement

- Unified analytics across all content
- Better understanding of audience engagement
- Data-driven content decisions

**Voice and Control**:
- All content remains JR Woodward's voice
- Full control over content creation and distribution
- No change to theological positions or content quality

**Existing Content**:
- All existing books remain as published
- All existing content remains accessible
- No requirement to change existing content

- Relationships with V3, Missio Alliance, Praxis Gathering remain intact
- Seminary teaching roles remain

- Conference speaking remains

- Co-founder roles (Missio Alliance, Praxis Gathering) remain

<!-- SOURCE: docs/movement_leader_research/jr-woodward/analysis/competitive-landscape.md -->

# Competitive Landscape Analysis: JR Woodward

**Research Date**: 2026-04-12
**Subject**: JR Woodward -- National Director, V3 Church Planting Movement
**Primary Niche**: Missional ecclesiology, polycentric leadership, theology of the powers, movement church planting
**Confidence Level**: High

---

## 1. Direct Competitors

These authors cover substantially identical territory -- missional ecclesiology and church planting -- with overlapping audiences.

### Dan White Jr.

- **Overlap**: Highest of any peer. Co-authored *The Church as Movement* (IVP, 2016). Co-leads V3 alongside Woodward. Both train church planters in the same eight competencies. Shared theological framework, shared audience, shared publisher relationships. Woodward wrote the foreword for White's *Subterranean* (2015).
- **Distinction**: White tilts toward the hyperlocal and the underground. *Subterranean: Why the Future of the Church Is Rootedness* (Cascade, 2015) and his Syracuse, NY context position him as a parish-scale practitioner-poet. Woodward is the systems thinker and academic; White is the storyteller and place-keeper.
- **Books**: 2 -- *Subterranean* (2015), *The Church as Movement* (2016, with Woodward)
- **Digital Presence**: Low. No prominent personal website, limited social media. Relies on V3 and Missio Alliance platforms.
- **Audience**: Small (3K-8K estimated). Overlaps almost entirely with Woodward's.
- **Unique Angle**: Rootedness theology, hyperlocal incarnational practice, the "underground" church metaphor.
- **Overlap with Woodward**: **Very High** -- co-author, co-leader. They are collaborative partners, not competitors.

### David Fitch

- **Overlap**: High. Fellow Missio Alliance board member, wrote foreword for *The Scandal of Leadership*. Both address missional theology, the Powers, and church culture. Fitch's *Faithful Presence* (2016) covers similar ground to Woodward's *Creating a Missional Culture* -- how should the church be organized for mission?
- **Distinction**: Fitch is a systematic theologian with an academic chair (B.R. Lindner Chair of Evangelical Theology, Northern Seminary). His work is more theologically dense and politically analytical (*The Church of Us vs. Them*, *Reckoning with Power*). He has a stronger Substack ("Fitch's Provocations") and a more public-facing intellectual voice. Fitch diagnoses ideology; Woodward diagnoses power structures and imitation patterns.
- **Books**: 7+ -- *The Great Giveaway* (2005), *The End of Evangelicalism?* (2011), *Faithful Presence* (2016), *The Church of Us vs. Them* (2019), *Reckoning with Power* (2024), plus edited volumes.
- **Digital Presence**: Moderate. Active Substack, Northern Seminary platform, Missio Alliance contributor, podcast appearances. Stronger personal digital presence than Woodward.
- **Audience**: Medium (15K-30K estimated). Seminary students, progressive evangelicals, pastors wrestling with political theology.
- **Unique Angle**: Political theology, ideology critique, "faithful presence" framework, post-Christendom evangelical identity.
- **Overlap with Woodward**: **High** -- shared theological ecosystem, shared board service, shared concern with power and mission. Fitch is more ideological analysis; Woodward is more leadership praxis.

### Brad Brisco

- **Overlap**: High. Both operate within missional-incarnational church planting networks. Brisco is Director of Multiplication Strategies at NAMB/Send Network. Both published through IVP's Forge Partnership line. Both engage Alan Hirsch's frameworks.
- **Distinction**: Brisco is denominationally embedded (SBC/NAMB) where Woodward is interdenominational (V3, which has Baptist roots but ecumenical practice). Brisco's breakout niche is covocational/bivocational church planting. Woodward is more focused on organizational culture and leadership formation.
- **Books**: 5 -- *Missional Essentials* (2012, with Ford), *The Missional Quest* (2014, with Ford), *Next Door As It Is in Heaven* (2016, with Ford), *Covocational Church Planting* (2021), *ReThink* (eBook).
- **Digital Presence**: Low. missionalchurchnetwork.com blog, modest social media (~132 Instagram followers), no newsletter, no courses, no YouTube.
- **Audience**: Small (5K-15K estimated). SBC church planters, bivocational ministers, Send Network trainees.
- **Unique Angle**: Covocational ministry as institutional strategy within a major denomination. The SBC-missional bridge.
- **Overlap with Woodward**: **High** -- church planting + missional culture. Different denominational context and different leadership focus (Brisco = vocational strategy, Woodward = organizational culture + powers).

### Hugh Halter

- **Overlap**: Moderate-High. Halter's *Tangible Kingdom* (2008) and incarnational community work overlap with Woodward's *Church as Movement*. Both advocate for neighborhood-rooted, non-institutional church forms. Both speak at Exponential and similar conferences.
- **Distinction**: Halter is a practitioner-storyteller (house painter turned church planter). His Lantern Network and Brave Cities give him a tangible movement infrastructure focused on post-Christian contexts. More embodied and experiential in tone; less systematic and academic than Woodward.
- **Books**: 7+ -- *The Tangible Kingdom* (2008), *Tangible Kingdom Primer* (2009), *AND: The Gathered and Scattered Church* (2010), *BIVO* (2013), *Flesh* (2014), *Righteous Brood*, *Happy Hour*.
- **Digital Presence**: Moderate. hughhalter.com, Brave Cities network, Outreach Magazine contributor, social media presence.
- **Audience**: Medium (15K-30K estimated). Church planters, bivocational ministers, missional community practitioners.
- **Unique Angle**: Incarnational embodiment, bivocational as lifestyle, tangible community as apologetic.
- **Overlap with Woodward**: **Moderate-High** -- incarnational community focus. Halter is more experiential/story-driven; Woodward is more systematic/framework-driven.

---

## 2. Adjacent Voices

These authors cover related territory but with a different angle, audience, or institutional context.

### Alan Hirsch

- **Relationship**: Mentor-tier figure. Hirsch wrote forewords for both *Creating a Missional Culture* and *The Church as Movement*. Woodward published *The Scandal of Leadership* through Hirsch's 100Movements Publishing. Both serve in the Movement Leaders Collective ecosystem. Hirsch praised Woodward's work as containing "missiological insights that only an apostolically inclined leader can bring."
- **Distinction**: Hirsch operates at the meta-framework level (APEST/5Q, movements theory, mDNA). Woodward applies and extends Hirsch's frameworks at the congregational and organizational level. Hirsch is the theorist; Woodward is the implementer-scholar.
- **Books**: 15+ including *The Forgotten Ways* (2006), *The Permanent Revolution* (2012, with Catchim), *5Q* (2017), *Reframation* (2019), *Metanoia* (2024).
- **Digital Presence**: Moderate. alanhirsch.org, 100Movements, Forge, 5Q Collective. Multiple organizational platforms. ~37,900 X followers, ~14,000 Facebook, Substack (1,500+). Wikipedia page.
- **Audience**: Large (50K-100K estimated). Movement leaders, denominational strategists, seminary students, global missional practitioners.
- **Unique Angle**: Movements meta-theory, APEST/5Q system, apostolic imagination.
- **Overlap with Woodward**: **High** (theological foundations) / **Low** (practical application). Hirsch is upstream -- Woodward applies his frameworks.

### Michael Frost

- **Relationship**: Adjacent thought leader and endorser. Frost endorsed *The Scandal of Leadership* ("Every Christian leader should read this") and *Creating a Missional Culture*. Both operate in the missional-incarnational stream.
- **Distinction**: Frost is Australian, global, and more prolific (20+ books). He co-founded the missional-incarnational paradigm with Hirsch (*The Shaping of Things to Come*, 2003). He is a missiologist-provocateur; Woodward is a missiologist-practitioner. Frost operates from Morling College's Tinsley Institute; Woodward from V3.
- **Books**: 20+ including *The Shaping of Things to Come* (2003, with Hirsch), *Exiles* (2006), *The Road to Missional* (2011), *Incarnate* (2014), *Surprise the World* (2016), *To Alter Your World* (2017).
- **Digital Presence**: Moderate. mikefrost.net. Migrating from X to Bluesky. Global conference circuit. Required reading in seminaries worldwide.
- **Audience**: Large (50K-100K estimated). Global seminary students, missional practitioners, Australian/international church leaders.
- **Unique Angle**: Post-Christendom missiology, incarnational provocation, global perspective, prolific output.
- **Overlap with Woodward**: **High** (theological) / **Low** (institutional). Frost is a tier above in visibility and breadth; Woodward is more embedded in North American movement infrastructure.

### Ed Stetzer

- **Relationship**: Institutional adjacent. Both serve the church planting practitioner community. Stetzer has endorsed and amplified voices in Woodward's network (foreword for Brisco/Ford's *The Missional Quest*). Both speak at Exponential.
- **Distinction**: Stetzer is a research-driven public intellectual with massive institutional reach (Dean at Talbot/Biola, Editor-in-Chief of Outreach Magazine, Moody Radio host, Lausanne regional director). He covers church planting but also culture, politics, and evangelicalism broadly. He is a generalist megaphone where Woodward is a specialist practitioner-scholar.
- **Books**: 12+ including *Planting Missional Churches* (2006, 2016 2nd ed.), *Breaking the Missional Code* (2006), *Christians in the Age of Outrage* (2018).
- **Digital Presence**: **Strongest of any peer.** @edstetzer on X (100K+ followers), Outreach Magazine platform, Moody Radio, ChurchLeaders.com.
- **Audience**: Very Large (200K+). Broad evangelical audience, church planters, pastors, seminary students.
- **Unique Angle**: Research-driven public evangelical intellectualism, institutional megaphone, culture-and-church commentary.
- **Overlap with Woodward**: **Moderate** -- overlaps on church planting only. Different scale, different scope, different theological posture.

### Neil Cole

- **Relationship**: Parallel track. Cole's "Organic Church" movement (2005) pioneered the simple/house church model that overlaps with Woodward's emphasis on smaller, neighborhood-rooted communities. Both advocate decentralized, multiplication-oriented ecclesiology.
- **Distinction**: Cole is more radical -- fully decentralized, house-church focused, no paid clergy as starting assumption. His Church Multiplication Associates claims 700+ churches in 32 states and 23 nations. Woodward works within more structured (though still non-traditional) movement frameworks through V3.
- **Books**: 10+ including *Organic Church* (2005), *Church 3.0* (2010), *Organic Leadership* (2009), *Primal Fire* (2014).
- **Digital Presence**: Low. Blog-based. Declining from peak influence years (2005-2012).
- **Audience**: Medium-declining (15K-30K estimated). Organic/simple church practitioners, house church networks.
- **Unique Angle**: Radical organic church, fully decentralized multiplication, no institutional overhead.
- **Overlap with Woodward**: **Moderate** -- both advocate multiplication and decentralization, but Woodward's model is more structured (V3 cohorts, polycentric leadership within community, not independent house churches).

### Mike Breen

- **Relationship**: Tangential. Breen's discipleship-first approach (*Building a Discipling Culture*) feeds the same formation pipeline. Both prioritize discipleship as the engine of mission.
- **Distinction**: Breen built a proprietary system (3DM, LifeShapes, Huddles) with its own publishing arm, training pipeline, and certification. More systemized and franchise-like than Woodward's organic, cohort-based V3 model. Breen's system has faced significant controversy regarding organizational culture -- ironic given Woodward's PhD work on leadership abuse and the Powers.
- **Books**: 6+ including *Building a Discipling Culture* (3 editions), *Multiplying Missional Leaders*, *Family on Mission*.
- **Digital Presence**: Moderate. 3dmovements.com, own publishing arm. Training-system focused.
- **Audience**: Medium (20K-40K estimated). Megachurch-adjacent leaders, discipleship program adopters.
- **Unique Angle**: Proprietary discipleship system, LifeShapes visual learning tools, structured multiplication.
- **Overlap with Woodward**: **Low** -- different system architecture, different ecclesial context, different leadership philosophy (Breen = centralized system; Woodward = polycentric, distributed).

### Dave Ferguson

- **Relationship**: Adjacent. Ferguson operates the church multiplication infrastructure (Exponential, formerly NewThing) that many of Woodward's V3 planters interface with. Both speak at Exponential conferences.
- **Distinction**: Ferguson is a mega-church pastor (Community Christian Church) turned movement CEO. His 2025 merger of NewThing into Exponential makes him the gatekeeper of the largest church planting conference ecosystem (~3,000 churches in network). More organizational/systems, less theological/missional than Woodward.
- **Books**: 8+ including *Exponential* (2010), *Hero Maker* (2018), *B.L.E.S.S.* (2021).
- **Digital Presence**: Strong. daveferguson.org, Exponential.org platform. Major conference circuit presence.
- **Audience**: Large (75K-150K estimated). Church planting practitioners across the spectrum.
- **Unique Angle**: Multiplication systems, movement infrastructure at scale, conference ecosystem gatekeeper.
- **Overlap with Woodward**: **Moderate** -- both advocate multiplication, but Ferguson operates at the systems/conference level while Woodward operates at the theology/formation level.

### Jeff Vanderstelt

- **Relationship**: Parallel. Vanderstelt's "Saturate" framework (missional communities, gospel fluency, everyday discipleship) overlaps substantially with Woodward's missional ecclesiology.
- **Distinction**: Vanderstelt is a church pastor (Doxa Church, Bellevue WA) with a tighter theological framework (gospel-centered, more Reformed). His Soma Family of Churches is a network of missional communities. More gospel-identity focused; Woodward is more missiology/movement-structure focused.
- **Books**: 3 -- *Saturate* (2015), *Gospel Fluency* (2017), *Making Space* (2019).
- **Digital Presence**: Moderate. saturatetheworld.com with training resources, podcast, field guides. Already has a unified content platform.
- **Audience**: Medium (20K-40K estimated). Reformed-leaning missional practitioners, Soma network churches.
- **Unique Angle**: Gospel fluency, missional communities within Reformed theological framework, Saturate platform.
- **Overlap with Woodward**: **Moderate** -- missional communities focus. Different theological home (Reformed vs. ecumenical missional) and different leadership model (Vanderstelt = gospel-centered pastoral; Woodward = polycentric APEST).

### Tim Catchim

- **Relationship**: Indirect collaborator through APEST ecosystem. Catchim co-authored *The Permanent Revolution* (2012) with Alan Hirsch, which is the foundational text on the apostolic function that Woodward's "Five Equippers" framework extends.
- **Distinction**: Catchim is focused specifically on APEST theory, typology development, and the apostolic/prophetic functions. More narrowly focused than Woodward, who applies APEST within a broader missional culture and movement ecclesiology framework.
- **Books**: 2 -- *The Permanent Revolution* (2012, with Hirsch), *The Permanent Revolution Playbook* (2014, with Hirsch).
- **Digital Presence**: Low-Moderate. Writing and consulting focused. Less public-facing than Woodward.
- **Audience**: Small (5K-10K estimated). APEST practitioners, 5Q enthusiasts, movement theorists.
- **Unique Angle**: APEST typology development, apostolic function theory.
- **Overlap with Woodward**: **Moderate** -- both extend APEST frameworks. Catchim is more theoretical; Woodward is more applied to organizational culture.

12. **Tim Catchim** -- Consulting-focused, limited public platform
13. **Dan White Jr.** -- Relies on V3 and Missio Alliance organizational platforms

---

## 4. Differentiation: What Makes JR Woodward Unique

### The Practitioner-Scholar at the Powers Intersection

Woodward occupies a position no other peer holds: he is the **only voice who has a PhD specifically on leadership abuse and the theology of the Powers, AND has 30+ years of grassroots church planting experience, AND leads a national church planting movement**. This three-way integration is unique:

- **Hirsch** provides the movement theory but does not lead a church planting movement directly
- **Fitch** has the academic chair and political theology but has not led a national movement infrastructure
- **Brisco** has the denominational church planting role but lacks the doctoral research on power and leadership
- **Halter** has the incarnational practice credibility but lacks the academic framework
- **Stetzer** has the institutional megaphone but has moved away from hands-on movement leadership
- **Breen** built a discipleship system but his organizational culture has been questioned -- making Woodward's *Scandal of Leadership* a direct response to the problems Breen's model exemplified

### The APEST Implementer

*Creating a Missional Culture* is recognized as "one of the most thorough developments" (Dr. Carlus Gupton) of the Ephesians 4:11 fivefold ministry framework for practical congregational application. While Hirsch and Catchim provide the APEST theory, Woodward provides the congregational implementation with his Five Equippers model (Dream Awakeners, Heart Revealers, Story Tellers, Soul Healers, Light Givers). No other author has made APEST as practically accessible for church teams.

### The Mimetic Theory Bridge

Woodward is the only author in this peer group who synthesizes Rene Girard's mimetic desire theory with Walter Wink's theology of the Powers and William Stringfellow's structural analysis, and then applies this synthesis to church leadership. This interdisciplinary move gives *The Scandal of Leadership* a unique intellectual foundation -- it is not just another "leadership ethics" book but a systematic diagnosis of why leaders fail, rooted in imitation theory.

### The Movement Infrastructure Leader

As National Director of V3, Woodward has direct training relationships with 1,000+ church planters. This is not a publishing relationship or conference-speaking relationship -- it is a cohort-based, 30-week formation relationship. V3's Praxis Community model is one of the most intensive church planter training pipelines in North America. Combined with his 7 co-founded organizations and 8 board roles, Woodward's network connectivity is among the highest in this peer group.

### Weaknesses Relative to Peers

| Weakness | Compared To |
|----------|-------------|
| Only 3 authored books (fewer than most peers) | Frost (20+), Stetzer (12+), Hirsch (15+), Cole (10+), Halter (7+) |
| Modest personal digital presence (15.8K X, 6.3K FB) | Stetzer (100K+), Hirsch (37.9K), Ferguson (strong platform) |
| Basic personal website (WordPress/Astra) | Vanderstelt (Saturate platform), Ferguson (Exponential), Breen (3DM) |
| No hosted podcast | Stetzer (Moody Radio), Vanderstelt (Saturate podcast) |
| Substack subscriber base is modest ("hundreds") | Hirsch (1,500+), Fitch (established Substack) |
| No assessment tool or diagnostic product | Hirsch (APEST assessment via 5Q), Breen (LifeShapes tools) |
| V3 training content not publicly digitized | Vanderstelt (Saturate resources), Breen (3DM training) |
| No Wikipedia page | Hirsch (has Wikipedia page) |

---

## 5. Movemental Implications

### Complement (Would Amplify Woodward on the Platform)

| Peer | Why They Complement | Network Synergy |
|------|-------------------|-----------------|
| **Alan Hirsch** | Provides the upstream movement theory (APEST, mDNA, movements) that Woodward applies. Hirsch on Movemental validates and contextualizes Woodward's work. Already deeply connected (forewords, publisher, MLC). | **Very High** -- natural learning pathway: Hirsch (movement theory) -> Woodward (culture + leadership) -> practitioner (implementation). |
| **Dan White Jr.** | Co-author and co-leader. Their content is already intertwined through *The Church as Movement* and V3. White on the platform creates the rootedness/hyperlocal complement to Woodward's systems-level thinking. | **Very High** -- collaborative partners. White's place-based narrative + Woodward's organizational framework = complete picture. |
| **Brad Brisco** | Different denominational context (SBC) with the same missional theology. Cross-pollination without competition. Brisco's covocational niche extends Woodward's movement ecclesiology into marketplace ministry. | **High** -- already in Movemental research pipeline. Same theological stream, different institutional context. |
| **Michael Frost** | The founding voice of the missional-incarnational stream. Frost on the platform anchors the entire theological family Woodward belongs to. No practical method competition. | **High** -- intellectual ancestor. Different hemisphere, complementary voice. |
| **Reggie McNeal** | Senior prophetic diagnostician. McNeal names the problems (present future, kingdom shift) that Woodward's V3 model solves. | **High** -- no overlap in practical method, strong overlap in theological diagnosis. |

### Compete (Would Create Tension or Audience Fragmentation)

| Peer | Why They Compete | Risk Level |
|------|-----------------|------------|
| **David Fitch** | Most direct intellectual competitor. Both address power, mission, and post-Christendom church. Both have active Substacks in the same niche (political theology + missional ecclesiology). Both serve on Missio Alliance board. | **Moderate** -- but manageable. Fitch is more systematic theology; Woodward is more leadership praxis. Could be positioned as "the theologian and the practitioner" within the same platform. |
| **Hugh Halter** | Overlapping incarnational community content. Halter's bivocational embodiment and Woodward's movement ecclesiology target similar readers with similar arguments about neighborhood-rooted church. | **Low-Moderate** -- Halter is storyteller, Woodward is framework-builder. Natural differentiation if curated. |
| **Jeff Vanderstelt** | Overlaps on missional community formation. Vanderstelt's Saturate platform already does what Movemental would do for Woodward. | **Low** -- Vanderstelt already has his own platform and a different theological home (Reformed). Unlikely to need Movemental. |
| **Mike Breen** | Breen's 3DM discipleship system competes for the same "how do we form disciples for mission" question. However, Breen's controversial organizational history makes *The Scandal of Leadership* a direct critique of Breen-style leadership failure. | **Low** -- different system, and Woodward's work is partly a response to the failures Breen's model exhibited. Not natural platform-mates. |

### Strategic Sequencing Recommendation

**Phase 1 (Foundation)**: Woodward + Hirsch + Dan White Jr. on the platform together. This creates the strongest V3/100Movements content ecosystem -- the movement theorist (Hirsch), the culture designer and leadership scholar (Woodward), and the hyperlocal practitioner (White). Natural cross-linking, shared vocabulary, established trust, and a complete theory-to-practice pipeline.

**Phase 2 (Expansion)**: Add Brisco, Frost, and McNeal. These voices expand the denominational range (Brisco brings the SBC bridge), international scope (Frost brings the global perspective), and generational wisdom (McNeal brings the senior prophetic voice) without competing for Woodward's specific niche. They create learning pathways and attract adjacent audiences.

**Phase 3 (Careful Addition)**: Consider Fitch and Halter. Position Fitch as "the political theologian" and Woodward as "the movement practitioner" within the same ecosystem. Position Halter as "the story" and Woodward as "the framework" for incarnational community.

**Avoid**: Bringing Stetzer or Ferguson onto the platform to amplify Woodward -- their audience scale would dwarf Woodward's niche. Better to leverage their platforms (Exponential conference, Outreach Magazine, Moody Radio) for outbound promotion of Woodward's Movemental content. Do not platform Breen alongside Woodward given the direct tension between Woodward's *Scandal of Leadership* thesis and Breen's organizational history.

---

## 6. Competitive Positioning Map

```
                    ACADEMIC / THEORETICAL
                           |
                   Frost   |   Hirsch
                           |
                  Fitch    |   Catchim
                           |
INDEPENDENT ---------------+--------------- INSTITUTIONAL
                           |
               WOODWARD    |   Brisco
                           |
            White  Halter  |   Stetzer
                  Cole     |   Ferguson
               Vanderstelt |   Breen
                           |
                    PRACTICAL / APPLIED
```

Woodward's unique quadrant: **Independent + Balanced (theory-practice)**. He is the only peer who combines academic rigor (PhD, ~274 citations) with movement infrastructure leadership (V3, 1,000+ planters trained) while remaining interdenominational and intellectually independent. He sits at the crossroads of the academic and the practical, the independent and the institutional.

---

## 7. Key Takeaway

JR Woodward's competitive advantage is not breadth of output or platform size -- on those metrics, he trails Hirsch, Frost, Stetzer, and Ferguson. His advantage is **unique intellectual depth combined with movement infrastructure**: he is the only voice who has produced a PhD-level diagnosis of leadership failure (theology of the Powers + mimetic theory), developed a practically implemented APEST framework (Five Equippers), co-founded 7 organizations, and currently trains 1,000+ church planters through a 30-week cohort model.

Movemental's opportunity is to give Woodward the digital infrastructure that matches his institutional and intellectual stature -- unified content hub, course delivery for V3's currently locked-away training content, audience building tools to scale beyond "hundreds" of Substack subscribers, and network amplification that makes visible the enormous collaborative ecosystem he has spent 30+ years building. The gap between Woodward's actual influence (7 organizations, 8 boards, 1,000+ trained planters, ~274 citations, IVP Book of the Year) and his digital visibility (3.3/5 Digital Presence Score, basic WordPress site, no podcast, no courses) is one of the largest in the Movemental research pipeline. Closing that gap is the opportunity.

---

*Analysis conducted: 2026-04-12*
*Sources: Web research, existing Movemental leader research files, publisher databases, Google Scholar*
